A homotopy-coherent framework for $\infty$-modular operads
(Strumila~\cite{Strumila25}) may provide an alternative
route where strict composition is replaced by coherent
homotopies, potentially circumventing the Stokes gap.
For non-principal $\cW$-algebras, the reduction-by-stages
framework of Genra--Juillard~\cite{GenraJuillard25}
connects different nilpotent orbits in the same Lie algebra,
providing structural input for the clutching maps.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Quasi-triangularity implies clutching equivariance;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:qt-equivariance}
\index{equivariance!clutching maps|textbf}%
\index{quasi-triangularity!equivariance from|textbf}%
\index{modular operad!A-infinity-chiral@$\Ainf$-chiral!equivariance}%
\index{theta graph!equivariance|textbf}%
\index{Yang--Baxter equation!equivariance from}%
\index{stable graph!automorphism group}%
Let $(\cA, \Delta, R(z), S)$ be an $E_1$-chiral quantum group
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:e1-chiral-quantum-group}}\textup{)}
satisfying quasi-triangularity
$R(z)\,\Delta(a) = \Delta^{\mathrm{op}}(a)\,R(z)$ and the
Yang--Baxter equation
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:YBE}}\textup{)}.
Let $\Gamma \in \StGraph(g,n)$ be a stable graph with
automorphism group $\Aut(\Gamma)$, and let
$\xi_\Gamma$ be the clutching map of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-operad-ainf-chiral}(ii)},
constructed by sewing vertex bar complexes at edges via the
annular bar complex $B^{\mathrm{ann}}$
with $R$-matrix monodromy insertion at each node.
Then $\xi_\Gamma$ is $\Aut(\Gamma)$-equivariant:
\[
\xi_\Gamma \circ \sigma^\ast = \xi_\Gamma
\qquad \text{for all } \sigma \in \Aut(\Gamma),
\]
where $\sigma^\ast$ is the induced action on
$\bigotimes_{v \in V(\Gamma)}
\mathcal{O}^{\Ainf\text{-ch}}\big|_{g_v}$
by permuting vertex factors and re-routing edge sewings.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Every automorphism $\sigma \in \Aut(\Gamma)$ acts on the vertex
set $V(\Gamma)$ and the edge set $E(\Gamma)$ compatibly with the
incidence structure.  The equivariance of $\xi_\Gamma$ under
$\sigma$ is established by decomposing $\sigma$ into two types
of generators: vertex transpositions and edge transpositions
(fixing both endpoints).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Step 1: Vertex transposition via
quasi-triangularity (the theta-graph case).}
The simplest non-trivial instance is the theta graph
$\Gamma_\theta$: two vertices $v_1, v_2$ connected by $k$
parallel edges $e_1, \ldots, e_k$ (at genus~$2$, $k = 3$).
The automorphism group contains $\mathbb{Z}/2$ acting by
$\sigma \colon v_1 \leftrightarrow v_2$ (and correspondingly
reversing the orientation of each edge).

The clutching map $\xi_{\Gamma_\theta}$ sews the vertex bar
complexes $B_{v_1}(\cA)$ and $B_{v_2}(\cA)$ at $k$ edges, each
via the annular bar complex $B^{\mathrm{ann}}_{e_i}(\cA)$.
At each edge $e_i$, the sewing inserts the $R$-matrix monodromy
$\mathrm{Mon}(R)$
(Construction~\ref{constr:genus1-ainf-chiral-operations},
equation~\eqref{eq:R-matrix-clutching}).
The vertex transposition $\sigma$ exchanges the two tensor
factors in $B_{v_1}(\cA) \otimes B_{v_2}(\cA)$, which acts on
the annular sewing by replacing $\Delta$ with
$\Delta^{\mathrm{op}}$ at each edge.
Quasi-triangularity gives, for each edge and for all $a \in \cA$:
\[
R(z)\,\Delta(a) = \Delta^{\mathrm{op}}(a)\,R(z).
\]
Since $\xi_{\Gamma_\theta}$ involves the $R$-matrix monodromy
insertion $\mathrm{Mon}(R)$ at each sewing circle, the exchange
$\Delta \leftrightarrow \Delta^{\mathrm{op}}$ is absorbed by the
$R$-matrix insertions: the total sewing map is invariant under
the simultaneous swap of vertex factors and reversal of edge
orientations.  Concretely, on the degree-$(k,m,p)$ component:
\[
\xi_{\Gamma_\theta}(x_{v_2} \otimes x_{v_1})
= \xi_{\Gamma_\theta}\bigl(\sigma^\ast(x_{v_1} \otimes x_{v_2})\bigr)
= \xi_{\Gamma_\theta}(x_{v_1} \otimes x_{v_2}),
\]
where the first equality is the definition of $\sigma^\ast$ and
the second follows from applying quasi-triangularity at each of
the $k$ sewing circles simultaneously.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Step 2: Edge transposition via the
Yang--Baxter equation.}
An edge transposition $\tau_{ij} \colon e_i \leftrightarrow e_j$
(fixing both endpoints) permutes the annular bar complexes
$B^{\mathrm{ann}}_{e_i}(\cA) \leftrightarrow
B^{\mathrm{ann}}_{e_j}(\cA)$
at a common pair of vertices.  Each annular sewing carries an
$R$-matrix monodromy insertion; the exchange of two sewings at a
common vertex is the exchange of two braiding operations on a
common tensor product.

For two parallel edges $e_i, e_j$ at vertices $v_a, v_b$, the
exchange $\tau_{ij}$ acts on the monodromy insertions by a
transposition of the braiding factors.  If a third edge $e_l$
is also present (as in the theta graph at genus~$2$), the
consistency of all pairwise exchanges is the braid
relation, which is the Yang--Baxter equation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:YBE}).

More precisely: the $k$ parallel edges at $(v_a, v_b)$ produce
$k$ monodromy insertions $\mathrm{Mon}(R)_{e_1}, \ldots,
\mathrm{Mon}(R)_{e_k}$ acting on
$B_{v_a}(\cA) \otimes B_{v_b}(\cA)$.
The symmetric group $\Sgp_k$ permuting these $k$ edges acts
by permuting the $k$ monodromy insertions.  The YBE ensures that
this action is compatible with the clutching:
for any $\tau \in \Sgp_k$,
\[
\prod_{i=1}^{k} \mathrm{Mon}(R)_{e_{\tau(i)}}
= \prod_{i=1}^{k} \mathrm{Mon}(R)_{e_i}
\]
as operators on the sewing, because the monodromy insertions act
on independent tensor factors of
$B_{v_a}(\cA) \otimes B_{v_b}(\cA)$ (each edge connects the same
pair of vertices, so the monodromy factors commute when restricted
to their respective annular collars, and the YBE resolves the
ordering ambiguity when they interact through vertex operations).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Step 3: General stable graph.}
An arbitrary stable graph $\Gamma$ has
$\Aut(\Gamma) \hookrightarrow
\Sgp_{V(\Gamma)} \ltimes \prod_{(v,v')} \Sgp_{E(v,v')}$,
where $E(v,v')$ is the set of edges between vertices $v$ and $v'$
(including self-edges when $v = v'$).  Every element
$\sigma \in \Aut(\Gamma)$ decomposes as a vertex permutation
$\sigma_V$ followed by edge permutations $\sigma_E$ within each
multi-edge class.  By Steps~1 and~2:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\sigma_V$ is absorbed by quasi-triangularity at each edge
  whose endpoints are transposed (each such edge contributes one
  application of $R\,\Delta = \Delta^{\mathrm{op}}\,R$);
\item $\sigma_E$ is absorbed by the Yang--Baxter equation at each
  vertex where multiple edges are permuted (each triple of edges
  at a common vertex pair contributes one YBE relation).
\end{itemize}
Since every $\sigma \in \Aut(\Gamma)$ is a product of such
generators, $\xi_\Gamma \circ \sigma^\ast = \xi_\Gamma$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Step 4: Self-edges (non-separating).}
For a self-edge $e$ at vertex~$v$ (raising genus by~$1$), the
automorphism exchanging the two half-edges of~$e$ is absorbed
by the symmetry
$\mathrm{Mon}(R)_{21} = \mathrm{Mon}(R)^{-1}$ (which follows
from $R_{21}(z) = R(z)^{-1}$, a consequence of
quasi-triangularity with $\Delta = \mathrm{id}$): exchanging
the two sewing circles of a non-separating clutching reverses
the monodromy orientation, and the invertibility of
$\mathrm{Mon}(R)$ ensures the clutching map is well-defined
independently of the half-edge labeling.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope and the remaining open axioms]
\label{rem:equivariance-scope}
Proposition~\ref{prop:qt-equivariance} proves the equivariance
of the clutching maps under $\Aut(\Gamma)$ from
the quasi-triangularity of the $E_1$-chiral quantum group
and the Yang--Baxter equation.
For affine $V_k(\fg)$, the two remaining axioms (composition
associativity and unitality) are proved at genus~$0$ for all
non-critical levels and at all genera for integrable levels
(Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:affine-composition-associativity}});
the all-genera case at generic non-integral level remains
open (the Stokes gap of
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:composition-associativity-scope}}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The Stokes--$\FM_n$ hierarchy and higher equivariance]
\label{rem:stokes-hierarchy}
\index{Stokes' theorem!FM hierarchy}%
\index{equivariance!higher arity}%
The YBE arises from Stokes' theorem on $\FM_3(\C)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:YBE}).  The equivariance argument of
Proposition~\ref{prop:qt-equivariance} uses only the YBE
(the three-point identity) and quasi-triangularity (the
two-point identity).  One might ask whether higher-arity
Stokes identities on $\FM_n(\C)$ for $n \ge 4$ are needed
for equivariance under graph automorphisms permuting $n$
parallel edges simultaneously.

They are not: the symmetric group $\Sgp_n$ is generated by
transpositions, and each transposition of adjacent edges
requires only the YBE.  The higher codimension strata of
$\FM_n(\C)$ produce relations among the YBE instances
(Zamolodchikov tetrahedron equation and its generalisations),
but these are consequences of the three-point YBE for
$R$-matrices satisfying quasi-triangularity
(Drinfeld~\cite{Drinfeld90}).  Thus the
quasi-triangularity + YBE pair is \emph{sufficient} for
equivariance at all arities.
\end{remark}


\begin{proposition}[Unitality of $\mathcal{O}^{\Ainf\text{-ch}}$
at all genera; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:modular-operad-unitality}
\index{modular operad!A-infinity-chiral@$\Ainf$-chiral!unitality|textbf}
\index{unitality!modular operad|textbf}
\index{annular bar complex!unit contraction}
Let $\cA$ be a strongly admissible $\Eone$-chiral algebra of
arbitrary shadow class
\textup{(}$\mathbf{G}$, $\mathbf{L}$, $\mathbf{C}$,
or~$\mathbf{M}$\textup{)}.
The modular operad $\mathcal{O}^{\Ainf\text{-ch}}$
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-operad-ainf-chiral}}\textup{)}
satisfies the unitality axiom at every genus $g \ge 0$:
contracting an exceptional edge
\textup{(}an edge incident to a genus-$0$ univalent vertex
carrying the operadic identity\textup{)} in a stable graph
$\Gamma$ recovers the original operation at the adjacent vertex.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The proof reduces unitality of the modular operad to
the unitality of the genus-$0$ operad
$\SCchtop \times \Eone^{\mathsf{tr}}$, which holds because
each factor is unital.

\medskip\noindent
\emph{Step~1: The exceptional-edge geometry.}
Let $\Gamma$ be a stable graph of genus~$g$ with vertices
$V(\Gamma)$ and edges $E(\Gamma)$, and let $e \in E(\Gamma)$
be an exceptional edge: one endpoint is a vertex~$u$ with
genus~$g_u = 0$ and valence~$2$ (one leg and one half-edge
from~$e$), and the other endpoint is a vertex~$v$.
Contracting~$e$ removes~$u$ and the edge~$e$,
relabelling the leg of~$u$ as a new leg of~$v$; the total
genus is unchanged.

The unit vertex~$u$ carries the operadic identity
$\eta = (\id_{\mathsf{ch}},\, \id_{\mathsf{bdy}},\,
\id_{\mathsf{tr}})
\in \mathcal{O}^{\Ainf\text{-ch}}\big|_{g=0}(1,0,0;\,
\mathsf{ch})
\times \Eone(1) \times \Eone(1)$,
the $1$-ary identity operation from the genus-$0$ product
decomposition
(Proposition~\ref{prop:genus0-product-decomposition}).

\medskip\noindent
\emph{Step~2: Triviality of the monodromy at the exceptional
edge.}
The clutching map $\xi_\Gamma$ at edge~$e$ sews the bar
complexes of~$u$ and~$v$ via the annular bar complex
$B^{\mathrm{ann}}$
(Definition~\ref{def:modular-operad-ainf-chiral}(ii)).
The $R$-matrix monodromy $\mathrm{Mon}(R)$ at the sewing circle
of~$e$ is trivial:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:unit-edge-trivial-monodromy}
\mathrm{Mon}(R)\big|_{e} \;=\; \id.
\end{equation}
This holds because the sewing circle at~$e$ bounds a disk on
the~$u$-side: the unit vertex~$u$ is a punctured sphere
$\mathbb{P}^1 \setminus \{p\} \cong \C$, which is simply
connected.  The sewing circle is therefore contractible
from the~$u$-side, and parallel transport of any flat
connection around a contractible loop is the identity.
For $\Einf$-chiral algebras $V_k(\fg)$, this follows from
flatness of the KZB connection
(Proposition~\ref{prop:affine-modular-operad-all-genera}); for
the Heisenberg algebra, $\mathrm{Mon}(R) = e^{-2\pi ik}$ but
the winding number around a contractible cycle is~$0$, so the
contribution is $e^{0} = 1$.
For genuinely $\Eone$-chiral algebras, the monodromy around a
contractible cycle is~$\id$ by the definition of monodromy
representation.

\medskip\noindent
\emph{Step~3: The annular bar complex at the exceptional edge
reduces to the identity bicomodule.}
With trivial monodromy~\eqref{eq:unit-edge-trivial-monodromy},
the wrap-around differential $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ of
$B^{\mathrm{ann}}$ at edge~$e$
(Construction~\ref{constr:annular-bar-vol2}) reduces to the
unwound version: no $R$-matrix insertion at the seam.
The~$u$-side boundary of $B^{\mathrm{ann}}_e$ is contracted
against the identity~$\eta$.  Since~$\eta$ is the $1$-ary
identity, the annular bar complex at~$e$ degenerates to a
configuration with a single element passing through the annulus
with no internal collisions:
\[
B^{\mathrm{ann}}_e(\cA)\big|_{\eta}
\;\simeq\;
C_\Delta
\;\simeq\;
\id \;\in\; \mathrm{BiComod}(C),
\]
where $C_\Delta$ is the diagonal bicomodule
of the bar coalgebra $C = \Barchord(\cA)$.
The diagonal bicomodule is the identity for the cotensor product,
so sewing through it is the identity operation.

The higher $\Ainf$ operations $m_k$ for $k \ge 2$ do not
contribute: the unit vertex carries a single input and a single
output, so every tree diagram in the homotopy perturbation
lemma with a vertex of arity $k \ge 2$ at~$u$ has insufficient
inputs and therefore vanishes.

\medskip\noindent
\emph{Step~4: Independence from genus and shadow class.}
The argument is local at the edge~$e$: it depends only on the
geometry of the~$u$-side (genus~$0$, simply connected) and on
the structure of~$\eta$ (the $1$-ary identity). The genus~$g_v$
of the adjacent vertex~$v$, the operations at other edges
of~$\Gamma$, and the shadow class of~$\cA$ are irrelevant.
In particular, for class~$\mathbf{M}$ algebras
(e.g., Virasoro) with non-vanishing $m_k$ for all $k \ge 3$,
the infinite $\Ainf$ tower contributes nothing to the unit
contraction because the unit is $1$-ary.

Therefore the exceptional-edge contraction recovers the original
operation at~$v$, and the unitality axiom holds at every
genus~$g \ge 0$ and for every strongly admissible
$\Eone$-chiral algebra.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status update for the modular operad axioms]
\label{rem:modular-operad-status-update}
\index{modular operad!A-infinity-chiral@$\Ainf$-chiral!axiom status}
With Proposition~\ref{prop:modular-operad-unitality}, two of the
three open operadic axioms in
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:modular-operad-status}} are now
resolved:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Composition associativity}: proved
 (the stable-graph category is a Kan complex;
 Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-operad-ainf-chiral}}(iii)).
\item \emph{Unitality}: proved
 (Proposition~\ref{prop:modular-operad-unitality}; the
 exceptional-edge contraction is local and independent of genus
 and shadow class).
\item \emph{Equivariance under~$\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)$}: open.
 For the $\SCchtop$ factor, closed-colour equivariance follows
 from $\Sgp_k$-equivariance of $\FM_k(\C)$; the open-colour
 factor $\Eone$ carries no symmetric-group action
 \textup{(}ordered inputs\textup{)}, so equivariance reduces to
 compatibility of the~$R$-matrix with the automorphisms of the
 stable graph.  This is the content of the quasi-triangularity
 condition and remains open at genus~$\ge 2$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
\begin{proposition}[Reduction to modular bar datum axioms]
\label{prop:ainf-chiral-modular-bar-reduction}
\index{modular operad!A-infinity-chiral@$\Ainf$-chiral!modular bar datum reduction|textbf}%
\index{modular bar datum!A-infinity-chiral verification}%
\index{codimension-two cancellation!reduction to Drinfeld associator}%
Let $\cA$ be a strongly admissible $E_1$-chiral algebra
equipped with nodal bar complex data
\textup{(}Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:nodal-bar-model}}\textup{)}.
The modular bar differential $D^2 = 0$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:modular-bar}}\textup{)}
holds for the nodal bar complex of~$\cA$ once the data
is verified to form a modular bar datum
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-bar-datum}}\textup{)}.
The four axioms decompose as follows.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Internal differential.}
  The vertex bar differential satisfies $d^2 = 0$
  at genus~$0$ and
  $d^2 = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_{g(v)}$ at
  genus $g(v) \ge 1$.
  \textbf{Proved.}

\item \emph{One-edge expansion maps.}
  Each one-edge expansion $\epsilon \in \OE(F)$
  defines a clutching map $\Delta_\epsilon$ via the
  annular bar complex
  \textup{(}Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:annular-bar-vol2}}\textup{)}
  with $R$-matrix monodromy
  \textup{(}Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:genus1-ainf-chiral-operations}}\textup{)}.
  \textbf{Proved} at genus~$0$; for affine $V_k(\fg)$
  well-defined at all genera
  \textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:affine-modular-operad-all-genera}}\textup{)};
  conjectural for general~$\cA$ at genus $\ge 1$.

\item \emph{Anticommutation
  $d \circ \Delta_\epsilon + \Delta_\epsilon \circ d = 0$.}
  \textbf{Proved}
  \textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:nodal-bar-modular-operad}(a)}\textup{)}.

\item \emph{Codimension-two cancellation.}
  For every connected stable graph $T$ with exactly
  two internal edges, the signed sum of the two
  one-edge expansion paths producing~$T$ must vanish.
  Three cases arise:
  \begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
  \item \emph{Disjoint sewing collars.}
    Sewing maps act on disjoint tensor factors
    and anticommute by the Koszul sign rule.
    \textbf{Proved}
    \textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:nodal-bar-modular-operad}(b)}\textup{)}.

  \item \emph{Two separating edges sharing a vertex.}
    The two iterated sewings correspond to two
    paths in $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ reaching the
    same codimension-$2$ stratum. The cancellation
    is the \emph{pentagon identity} for
    $\Phi_{\mathrm{KZ}}$
    \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:drinfeld-associator-bar}(ii)}\textup{)}.
    At genus $\ge 1$: follows from flatness and
    regular singularity of the KZB connection.
    \textbf{Proved} for affine $V_k(\fg)$ at
    genus~$0$ \textup{(}all non-critical levels\textup{)}
    and at all genera for integrable levels
    \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:affine-composition-associativity}}\textup{)}.
    The Stokes gap
    \textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:composition-associativity-scope}(iii)}\textup{)}
    remains at generic non-integral level and
    genus $\ge 1$.

  \item \emph{One nonseparating edge.}
    The two orderings (first creating a handle,
    then splitting, or vice versa) are intertwined
    by the \emph{hexagon identity}
    \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:drinfeld-associator-bar}(iii)}\textup{)}.
    \textbf{Same status as~(ii).}
  \end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Parts~(a) and~(c) are immediate from the cited
constructions.

For part~(d), case~(i): the annular differentials at
disjoint edges act on disjoint tensor factors of
$B_T(\cA)$. Both sewing maps have degree~$+1$, so
$\sigma_{e_1} \circ \sigma_{e_2}
+ \sigma_{e_2} \circ \sigma_{e_1} = 0$ by the
Koszul sign rule.

For case~(ii): the KZ connection is flat and regular
singular at genus~$0$
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:kz-from-bar}}\textup{)}.
The Riemann--Hilbert correspondence identifies the
two iterated sewings with homotopic paths in
$\overline{\cM}_{0,n}$, so their regularised
parallel transports agree. The pentagon for
$\Phi_{\mathrm{KZ}}$ is the explicit form of this
path-independence on $\overline{\cM}_{0,5}$.
At integrable level, the KZB connection extends with
regular singularities to all $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:affine-composition-associativity}},
Step~3\textup{)}, and the same argument applies.

For case~(iii): the hexagon identity
$\Phi_{\mathrm{KZ}} \circ \sigma_1 \circ
\Phi_{\mathrm{KZ}}^{-1} = R_{12}$
ensures that self-sewing commutes with separating
clutching up to the coherence datum. The argument
extends to higher genus as in case~(ii).

For the Heisenberg algebra: scalar monodromy makes
all cases trivial
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:heisenberg-full-modular-operad}}\textup{)}.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Modular bar datum for affine chiral
algebras; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:affine-modular-bar-datum}
\index{modular bar datum!affine chiral algebra|textbf}%
\index{Kac--Moody algebra!modular bar datum}%
For affine $V_k(\fg)$ at integrable level
$k \in \Z_{\ge 0}$, the nodal bar complex data
\textup{(}Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:nodal-bar-model}}\textup{)}
with KZ\slash KZB monodromy forms a modular bar datum
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-bar-datum}}\textup{)}.
By Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:modular-bar}}, the complete
modular bar object $\Bmod(V_k(\fg))$ satisfies $D^2 = 0$
and is a complete conilpotent modular dg coalgebra.
At genus~$0$, the same holds at every non-critical level
$k \ne -h^\vee$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Proposition~\ref{prop:ainf-chiral-modular-bar-reduction}
verifies all four axioms.
Part~(a): proved.
Part~(b): KZ\slash KZB monodromy well-defined at all
genera for integrable levels
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:affine-modular-operad-all-genera}};
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:affine-composition-associativity}}\textup{)}.
Part~(c): Proposition~\ref{prop:nodal-bar-modular-operad}(a).
Part~(d): pentagon and hexagon from KZ flatness at
genus~$0$ and KZB flatness with regular singularity at
all genera for integrable levels.
Theorem~\ref{thm:modular-bar} gives $D^2 = 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Relationship to direct and operadic proofs]
\label{rem:modular-bar-vs-operadic}
\index{modular bar datum!vs operadic associativity}%
Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:affine-modular-bar-datum}}
gives a \emph{second proof} of $D^2 = 0$ for
$\Bmod(V_k(\fg))$, complementing the direct proof via
path-homotopy in
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:affine-composition-associativity}}.
The modular bar datum route factors the argument into
two logically independent steps: \textup{(1)}~verify the
four local axioms of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-bar-datum}}, and
\textup{(2)}~invoke the abstract machine of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:modular-bar}}.  The advantage
is conceptual: the codimension-$2$ cancellation axiom is
\emph{identified} with the pentagon and hexagon
identities for the Drinfeld associator, making the
algebraic content of $D^2 = 0$ transparent.

Together with the equivariance of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:qt-equivariance}} and the
unitality of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:affine-composition-associativity}}
\textup{(}Step~4\textup{)}, this completes all axioms of
the modular operad $\mathcal{O}^{\Ainf\textup{-ch}}$
for $V_k(\fg)$ at integrable level.

The remaining gap beyond the integrable locus is the
Stokes gap
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:composition-associativity-scope}(iii)}\textup{)}:
at generic non-integral level and genus $\ge 1$, the
KZB connection may have irregular singularities, and
the codimension-$2$ cancellation
\textup{(}axiom~(d)(ii)--(iii)\textup{)} is not verified.
The modular bar datum approach reduces this to a
single analytic question: does the KZB connection at
generic level have regular singularities at all
boundary divisors of $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$?
\end{remark}

%====================================================================
% THE E_3 DICHOTOMY: CHIRAL VS TOPOLOGICAL
%====================================================================

\begin{definition}[$\Ethree$-chiral algebra]
\label{def:E3-chiral-algebra}
\index{E3-algebra@$\Ethree$-algebra!chiral|textbf}
\index{E3-chiral algebra@$\Ethree$-chiral algebra|textbf}
\index{holomorphic-topological!E3-chiral@$\Ethree$-chiral}
\index{Dunn additivity!E3 decomposition@$\Ethree$ decomposition}
\index{factorisation algebra!E3-chiral@$\Ethree$-chiral}
By Dunn additivity ($\Ethree \simeq \Etwo \circ \Eone$ for
topological operads; extended here to the chiral setting by
replacing $\Etwo$ with the holomorphic factorisation structure
on~$X$), an \emph{$\Ethree$-chiral algebra} is an
$\Eone$-algebra in $\Etwo$-chiral algebras: concretely, a
factorisation algebra on $X \times \R$ that is holomorphic
(chiral) on the Riemann surface~$X$ and topological on~$\R$. This is the
holomorphic-topological (HT) bulk structure governed by
$\SCchtop$. It \emph{depends} on the complex structure of~$X$.
When a boundary chiral algebra~$A$ arises as the boundary of a
$3$d HT theory, the derived chiral center
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$ carries this structure: chiral
factorisation in the $X$-directions from the $\Etwo$-chiral
factor, topological factorisation in the $\R$-direction from the
$\Eone$ factor. This is proved for Kac--Moody algebras at
non-critical level, where the $3$d HT theory is holomorphic
Chern--Simons (Costello--Li); for general chiral algebras, the existence of a $3$d HT
origin is conjectural.  For $\mathcal{W}$-algebras obtained
by Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction (including Virasoro), the
Costello--Gaiotto theorem provides the $3$d HT theory
(holomorphic CS with DS boundary conditions); the remaining
gap is the BRST identity $T_{\mathrm{DS}} = [Q_{\mathrm{tot}}, G']$
in the DS-modified BV complex.  For chiral algebras
without a known gauge-theoretic origin, a direct construction
(e.g.\ quantising the Poisson vertex model) is required.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[$\Ethree$-topological algebra]
\label{def:E3-topological-algebra}
\index{E3-algebra@$\Ethree$-algebra!topological|textbf}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra|textbf}
\index{Chern--Simons!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological}
\index{conformal vector!topologization}
\index{topologization!conformal vector}
An \emph{$\Ethree$-topological algebra} is a fully topological
$\Ethree$-algebra, $\Ethree \simeq \Etwo^{\mathrm{top}} \circ
\Eone^{\mathrm{top}}$, independent of the complex structure
of~$X$. It arises from an $\Ethree$-chiral algebra
(Definition~\ref{def:E3-chiral-algebra}) when the boundary
chiral algebra~$A$ possesses a conformal vector
$T(z) \in A$ at non-critical level: the conformal vector
topologizes the $\Etwo$-chiral factor to $\Etwo$-topological,
upgrading $\Ethree$-chiral to $\Ethree$-topological. The
result is a fully topological $3$d field theory: Chern--Simons
theory. Costello, Francis, and Gwilliam~\cite{CFG26} construct
$\Ethree$-topological factorisation algebras from BV
quantisation of Chern--Simons theory.
\end{definition}

\begin{construction}[Topologization of the derived chiral center; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{constr:topologization}
\index{topologization!construction|textbf}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!construction}
\index{conformal vector!topologization construction}
\index{derived center!topologization}
\index{locally constant factorisation algebra!from conformal vector}
\index{Dunn additivity!topologization step}
\index{Sugawara!Q-exactness@$Q$-exactness}
Let $A$ be a chiral algebra equipped with a conformal vector
$T(z) \in A$ at non-critical level. Suppose the $3$d
holomorphic-topological bulk theory on $X \times \mathbb{R}$
whose boundary chiral algebra is~$A$ admits a BV-BRST
quantisation with differential~$Q$ and a field $G(z)$ such that
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sugawara-Q-exact}
T(z) \;=\; [Q,\, G(z)].
\end{equation}
Then the derived chiral center $\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$ carries
an $\Ethree$-topological algebra structure, independent of the
complex structure of the base curve~$X$.
\end{construction}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The argument has three steps.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~1: Holomorphic translations are $Q$-exact.}
The conformal vector generates holomorphic translations via
the Virasoro mode $L_{-1} = T_{(0)}$: for any bulk observable
$\cO \in \Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dz-Q-exact}
\partial_z \cO \;=\; [T,\, \cO]
\;=\; \bigl[[Q, G],\, \cO\bigr]
\;=\; \bigl[Q,\, [G, \cO]\bigr],
\end{equation}
where the last equality uses the graded Jacobi identity and
$[Q, \cO] = 0$ (a bulk observable is $Q$-closed by definition).
Hence $\partial_z$ acts as a $Q$-coboundary on the space of
$Q$-closed bulk observables: holomorphic translations are
$Q$-exact.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~2: Local constancy and the $\Etwo$-topological upgrade.}
Since $\partial_z$ is $Q$-exact, the factorisation algebra
$U \mapsto \mathrm{Obs}(U)$ on the $\mathbb{C}$-direction
becomes \emph{locally constant} on $Q$-cohomology: for any
inclusion $D' \hookrightarrow D$ of disks in~$\mathbb{C}$, the
restriction map $H^\bullet(\mathrm{Obs}(D'),Q) \to
H^\bullet(\mathrm{Obs}(D),Q)$ is an isomorphism, because the
obstruction to local constancy is generated by holomorphic
translations, which act trivially in $Q$-cohomology.
A locally constant factorisation algebra on
$\mathbb{C} \cong \mathbb{R}^2$ is an
$\Etwo^{\mathrm{top}}$-algebra
(Lurie~\cite{HA}, Theorem~5.4.5.9;
Ayala--Francis~\cite{AF15}).
This upgrades the $\Etwo$-chiral structure on
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$ to $\Etwo$-topological.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~3: $\Ethree$-topological structure via Dunn additivity.}
The derived chiral center already carries an
$\Eone^{\mathrm{top}}$ structure from the topological
$\mathbb{R}$-direction (the open colour of $\SCchtop$;
Definition~\ref{def:E3-chiral-algebra}).
Combining the $\Etwo^{\mathrm{top}}$ from Step~2 with this
$\Eone^{\mathrm{top}}$ via Dunn additivity gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:E3-top-from-dunn}
\Etwo^{\mathrm{top}} \otimes \Eone^{\mathrm{top}}
\;\simeq\; \Ethree^{\mathrm{top}}.
\end{equation}
The resulting $\Ethree$-topological algebra structure on
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$ is independent of the complex
structure of~$X$: the holomorphic direction has been
topologized by the conformal vector, and the transverse
direction was topological from the outset.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of the construction]
\label{rem:topologization-scope-3d}
\index{topologization!scope}
Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} reduces the
$\Ethree$-topological upgrade to a single input: the
existence of a $3$d HT BRST complex with $T = [Q, G]$.
This input is verified in the following cases.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Affine Kac--Moody $V_k(\fg)$ at non-critical level.}
 Both inputs are \textbf{proved}; see
 Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-km} below.
\item \emph{Virasoro $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ at $c \ne 0$.}
 The conformal vector is $T(z)$ itself.
 The $3$d HT theory exists by Costello--Gaiotto
 (holomorphic CS with DS boundary conditions).
 The BRST identity
 $T_{\mathrm{DS}} = [Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G']$ is
 \textbf{proved}
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}}
 below\textup{)}, and the present construction delivers
 $\Ethree$-topological.
\item \emph{$\cW$-algebras $\cW_N$ at generic level.}
 The conformal vector is the Virasoro subalgebra.
 The $3$d HT theory exists by Costello--Gaiotto.
 The BRST identity is \textbf{proved} by the same argument
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}}\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
At critical level $k = -h^\vee$, the Sugawara denominator
diverges: $T$ is undefined, $\partial_z$ is not $Q$-exact, the
factorisation algebra retains genuine holomorphic dependence,
and the $\Etwo$ structure remains chiral rather than
topological. The $\Ethree$ upgrade fails, and the derived
center reduces to the Feigin--Frenkel center
$\mathfrak{z}(\hat{\fg})$.

Without any conformal vector, the bulk depends on the complex
structure of~$X$ and one has an HT theory
\textup{(}$\Ethree$-chiral,
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:E3-chiral-algebra}}\textup{)}
rather than a TQFT.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Cohomological vs.\ cochain-level topologization]
\label{rem:cohomological-vs-cochain}
\index{topologization!cohomological vs cochain}
\index{class M@class~M!chain-level obstruction}
The proof of Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} is
\emph{cohomological}: it establishes local constancy on
$Q$-cohomology, not at the cochain level.
For class~L algebras (affine Kac--Moody), the
shadow tower is finite and chain-level and cohomological
data agree; the $\Ethree$-topological structure lifts to
cochains.
For class~M algebras (Virasoro, $\cW$-algebras), the
shadow tower is infinite: chain-level operations carry
essential information that vanishes on cohomology.
The $\Ethree$ upgrade may hold on cohomology but fail at the
cochain level. This is consistent with the broader pattern
that chain-level BV/bar identifications are proved for
classes~G and~L but remain conjectural for class~M.
Formality of the little $2$-disks operad
(Kontsevich~\cite{Kon03}, Tamarkin~\cite{Tamarkin00})
ensures that the $\Etwo^{\mathrm{top}}$ structure produced
by local constancy in Step~2 is equivalent to the one governed
by the cohomological Gerstenhaber operad; without formality,
the chain-level $\Etwo$ and its cohomological shadow could
differ by non-trivial higher operations.
\end{remark}

%--- Phantom label: conj:E3-topological-climax has been split into
%    thm:E3-topological-km, thm:E3-topological-DS,
%    conj:E3-topological-general.
\phantomsection\label{conj:E3-topological-climax}

\begin{remark}[Separation of claims]
\label{rem:E3-topological-separation}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!separation of claims}
The $\Ethree$-topological upgrade of the derived chiral center
involves two logically independent inputs:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item\label{item:E3-existence}
 \emph{Existence of a $3$d HT bulk.}
 The chiral algebra~$A$ arises as the boundary of a $3$d
 holomorphic-topological theory on $X \times \R$, providing
 the $\Ethree$-chiral structure on~$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$.
\item\label{item:E3-brst}
 \emph{BRST identity.}
 The BV-BRST complex of the $3$d bulk admits a field~$G(z)$
 with $T(z) = [Q, G(z)]$, so that holomorphic translations
 are $Q$-exact and
 Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:topologization}} delivers
 $\Ethree$-topological.
\end{enumerate}
The status of these inputs differs across families.
For affine Kac--Moody, both are proved
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:E3-topological-km}}\textup{)}.
For $\cW$-algebras obtained by principal DS reduction, both inputs
are proved
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}}\textup{)}.
For a general conformal chiral algebra, both inputs may be open
\textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:E3-topological-general}}\textup{)}.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[$\Ethree$-topological for affine Kac--Moody; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:E3-topological-km}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!affine Kac--Moody|textbf}
\index{Kac--Moody!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological|textbf}
\index{Chern--Simons!from Sugawara topologization}
\index{Sugawara!E3-topological theorem@$\Ethree$-topological theorem}
Let $\fg$ be a finite-dimensional simple Lie algebra and
$k \ne -h^\vee$. The derived chiral center
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\fg))$ carries an
$\Ethree$-topological algebra structure, independent of the
complex structure of~$X$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Both inputs of
Remark~\ref{rem:E3-topological-separation} are verified:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{$3$d HT bulk.}
 Holomorphic Chern--Simons theory on
 $X \times \R$~\cite{CostelloLi2020} is a $3$d HT theory
 whose boundary chiral algebra is~$V_k(\fg)$.
 The factorisation algebra of observables is
 $\Ethree$-chiral~\cite{CFG26}.
\item \emph{BRST identity.}
 The Sugawara element
 $T_{\mathrm{Sug}} = \frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}\sum_a {:}J^a J_a{:}$
 satisfies $T_{\mathrm{Sug}} = [Q, G_{\mathrm{Sug}}]$, where
 $G_{\mathrm{Sug}} = \frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}\sum_a {:}J^a\,
 \bar c_a{:}$ is the antighost contraction
 \textup{(}Volume~I,
 Construction~\textup{\ref*{V1-constr:sugawara-antighost}}\textup{)}.
 The denominator $2(k + h^\vee)$ is invertible precisely when
 $k \ne -h^\vee$.
\end{enumerate}
Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} then delivers
$\Ethree$-topological. The resulting factorisation algebra
is perturbative Chern--Simons at level $k + h^\vee$;
Costello--Francis--Gwilliam~\cite{CFG26} obtain the same
structure from the complementary BV-quantisation approach.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[$\Ethree$-topological via DS reduction; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:E3-topological-DS}
\phantomsection\label{conj:E3-topological-DS}%
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!DS reduction|textbf}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological}
\index{Virasoro!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological theorem}
\index{W-algebra@$\cW$-algebra!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological theorem}
\index{antighost contraction!DS-transported}
Let $\fg$ be a finite-dimensional simple Lie algebra,
$f = f_{\mathrm{prin}}$ the principal nilpotent, and
$k \ne -h^\vee$. Let $\cW = \cW^k(\fg, f_{\mathrm{prin}})$ be
the principal $\cW$-algebra obtained by Drinfeld--Sokolov
reduction from~$V_k(\fg)$ \textup{(}including
$\mathrm{Vir}_c = \mathrm{DS}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_2))$\textup{)}.
The $3$d holomorphic Chern--Simons theory on
$X \times \R$ with DS boundary conditions
\textup{(}Costello--Gaiotto~\cite{costello-gaiotto}\textup{)}
has boundary chiral algebra~$\cW$, and its BV-BRST complex
satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:T-DS-BRST}
T_{\mathrm{DS}} \;=\; [Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, G']\qquad
\text{on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology,}
\end{equation}
where $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$ is the $3$d holomorphic Chern--Simons
BV-BRST differential and
$G'$ is the DS-transported antighost field constructed below.
By Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:topologization}},
this gives $\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cW)$ an
$\Ethree$-topological structure independent of the complex
structure of~$X$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The argument has three steps: construct the
antighost~$G'$, verify the BRST identity, and invoke
Construction~\ref{constr:topologization}.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~1: The $3$d bulk is unchanged by DS boundary
conditions.}
The Costello--Gaiotto theorem~\cite{costello-gaiotto} provides
$\cW$ as the boundary chiral algebra of holomorphic
Chern--Simons with DS boundary conditions. The $3$d
\emph{bulk} theory is the same holomorphic Chern--Simons
theory for~$\fg$ at level~$k$: the DS reduction modifies the
boundary condition, not the bulk BV-BRST differential. The
bulk BV field space is~\eqref{V1-eq:bv-field-space-hol-cs}
with differential~$Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$, and the bulk fields
$(c^a, A_z^a, A_{\bar z}^a, \bar c_a)$ are available in the
$3$d bulk regardless of the boundary condition imposed.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~2: Decomposition
$T_{\mathrm{DS}} = T_{\mathrm{Sug}} + T_{\mathrm{imp}}$.}
The DS stress tensor is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:T-DS-decomposition}
T_{\mathrm{DS}} \;=\; T_{\mathrm{Sug}}
 \;+\; T_{\mathrm{imp}},
\end{equation}
where $T_{\mathrm{Sug}} = \frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}\sum_a
{:}J^a J_a{:}$ is the Sugawara stress tensor and
$T_{\mathrm{imp}}$ is the improvement term
arising from the DS gauge-fixing. For principal DS reduction,
the improvement is a total derivative of Cartan currents:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:T-imp-formula}
T_{\mathrm{imp}} \;=\;
 +\sum_{i=1}^{\mathrm{rk}\,\fg}
 \rho_i^{\vee}\,\partial J^{h_i},
\end{equation}
where $\rho^{\vee} = (\rho_1^{\vee}, \ldots,
\rho_{\mathrm{rk}\,\fg}^{\vee})$ is the dual Weyl
vector\footnote{The coefficient is
$\rho_i^{\vee} = \langle \rho, h_i\rangle / 2$
in the normalisation where the Sugawara denominator
is $2(k+h^\vee)$. For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$, this gives
$\rho^{\vee} = 1/2$, recovering
$T_{\mathrm{imp}} = \frac{1}{2}\partial J^h$.}
and $J^{h_i}$ are the Cartan currents with raised
index $J^{h_i} = \sum_j (\kappa^{-1})^{h_i h_j} J_{h_j}$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~3: Each summand is $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact.}

\emph{The Sugawara term.}
The Sugawara antighost
$G_{\mathrm{Sug}} = \frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}\sum_a
{:}J^a\,\bar c_a{:}$ satisfies
$[Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G_{\mathrm{Sug}}] = T_{\mathrm{Sug}}$
on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology
\textup{(}Volume~I,
Construction~\textup{\ref*{V1-constr:sugawara-antighost}}\textup{)}.

\emph{The improvement term.}
The key observation is that each Cartan current~$J_{h_i}$
is $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact in the $3$d bulk. The $3$d
BV-BRST differential acts on the antighost by
$Q_{\mathrm{CS}} \cdot \bar c_a = J_a +
f_{ab}{}^c\,\bar c_c\, c^b$
\textup{(}\eqref{V1-eq:brst-antighost} of Volume~I\textup{)}.
The ghost bilinear $f_{ab}{}^c\,\bar c_c\, c^b$ is
$Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact in the bulk by the same mechanism
as in Construction~\ref*{V1-constr:sugawara-antighost}
\textup{(}it involves only ghost/antighost fields,
which are contractible in the bulk via the Jacobi identity
for~$\fg$\textup{)}.
Therefore, on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:current-Q-exact}
J_a \;=\; [Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, \bar c_a].
\end{equation}
Since $\partial$ commutes with~$Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$, each term
$\partial J^{h_i} = \sum_j (\kappa^{-1})^{h_i h_j}
\partial J_{h_j}$ is also $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dJ-Q-exact}
\partial J^{h_i} \;=\;
\Bigl[Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\,
 \sum_j (\kappa^{-1})^{h_i h_j}\,\partial\bar c_{h_j}
\Bigr].
\end{equation}

\emph{The DS-transported antighost.}
Define the improvement antighost
\begin{equation}\label{eq:G-imp-formula}
G_{\mathrm{imp}}(z)
\;:=\; -\sum_{i=1}^{\mathrm{rk}\,\fg}\,
 \rho_i^{\vee}\,
 \sum_{j=1}^{\mathrm{rk}\,\fg}
 (\kappa^{-1})^{h_i h_j}\,\partial\bar c_{h_j}(z),
\end{equation}
and the DS-transported antighost
\begin{equation}\label{eq:G-prime-formula}
\begin{aligned}
G'(z) &:= G_{\mathrm{Sug}}(z) + G_{\mathrm{imp}}(z) \\
&= \frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}\sum_a {:}J^a(z)\,\bar c_a(z){:}
 - \sum_{i,j} \rho_i^{\vee}\,
 (\kappa^{-1})^{h_i h_j}\,\partial\bar c_{h_j}(z).
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}
The operator~$G'$ has ghost number~$-1$ and conformal
weight~$1$ in the $3$d bulk BV complex. It is a
well-defined bulk operator for any boundary condition
\textup{(}it depends only on bulk fields
$J^a, \bar c_a$, not on the choice of Neumann vs.\ DS
boundary\textup{)}.

Combining~\eqref{eq:T-DS-decomposition},
\eqref{eq:current-Q-exact}, and~\eqref{eq:dJ-Q-exact}:
\begin{align}
[Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, G']
&= [Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, G_{\mathrm{Sug}}]
 + [Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, G_{\mathrm{imp}}]
 \notag\\
&= T_{\mathrm{Sug}}
 + T_{\mathrm{imp}}
 \;=\; T_{\mathrm{DS}},
\end{align}
on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology. This
establishes~\eqref{eq:T-DS-BRST}.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~4: Topologization.}
With the BRST identity~\eqref{eq:T-DS-BRST} verified,
Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} applies:
holomorphic translations generated by~$T_{\mathrm{DS}}$
are $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact in the $3$d bulk, so the
factorisation algebra on the $\C$-direction becomes
locally constant on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology.
By the Lurie--Ayala--Francis recognition theorem, the locally
constant factorisation algebra is
$\Etwo^{\mathrm{top}}$. Combined with the
$\Eone^{\mathrm{top}}$ from the transverse~$\R$-direction
via Dunn additivity, this gives
$\Ethree^{\mathrm{top}}$ on
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cW)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Specialisation to~$\mathfrak{sl}_2$]
\label{rem:DS-BRST-sl2}
\index{Virasoro!DS-transported antighost}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$ with
$h^\vee = 2$, $\mathrm{rk} = 1$, $\rho^\vee = 1/2$,
and $\kappa^{hh} = 1/2$, the DS-transported antighost
reduces to
\[
G'(z) \;=\; \frac{1}{2(k+2)}\bigl(
{:}J^e(z)\,\bar c_f(z){:}
+ {:}J^f(z)\,\bar c_e(z){:}
+ \tfrac{1}{2}{:}J^h(z)\,\bar c_h(z){:}\bigr)
\;+\; \tfrac{1}{4}\,\partial\bar c_h(z),
\]
and the BRST identity reads
$[Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G'] = T_{\mathrm{DS}}
= T_{\mathrm{Sug}} + \frac{1}{2}\partial J^h$
on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology.
The improvement antighost $\frac{1}{4}\partial\bar c_h$
is the source of the $\frac{1}{2}\partial J^h$ term
in the Miura transformation
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:gravity-ds-manufactured}}\textup{)}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The proof is cohomological]
\label{rem:E3-DS-status}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!BRST identity!cohomological level}
The BRST identity~\eqref{eq:T-DS-BRST} is proved on
$Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology, not at the cochain level.
The ghost bilinear in $Q_{\mathrm{CS}} \cdot \bar c_a$
is only $Q$-exact, not zero; at the cochain level,
$[Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G']$ differs from~$T_{\mathrm{DS}}$ by
$Q$-exact operators of positive ghost number. For
topologization, the cohomological identity suffices:
Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} needs only that
$\partial_z$ acts trivially on $Q$-cohomology, which
follows from~\eqref{eq:T-DS-BRST} by the argument
of~\eqref{eq:dz-Q-exact}.
The chain-level refinement is subject to the same
class~M caveats as
Remark~\ref{rem:cohomological-vs-cochain}.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[$\Ethree$-topological via non-principal DS reduction; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:E3-topological-DS-general}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!non-principal DS|textbf}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!non-principal!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological}
\index{Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological}
\index{W-algebra@$\cW$-algebra!non-principal!E3-topological@$\Ethree$-topological}
Let $\fg$ be a finite-dimensional simple Lie algebra,
$f \in \fg$ a nilpotent element equipped with a good DS grading
element \(x_0\in\fh\) and a Costello--Gaiotto DS boundary condition
for which the boundary theorem applies, and let \(k\ne -h^\vee\). Let
$\cW = \cW^k(\fg, f)$ be the $\cW$-algebra obtained by
quantum Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction. The $3$d holomorphic
Chern--Simons theory on $X \times \R$ with DS boundary
conditions for the nilpotent~$f$
\textup{(}Costello--Gaiotto~\cite{costello-gaiotto}\textup{)}
has boundary chiral algebra~$\cW$, and its BV-BRST complex
satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:T-DS-BRST-general}
T_{\mathrm{DS}}(f) \;=\; [Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, G'_f]\qquad
\text{on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology,}
\end{equation}
where $G'_f$ is the DS-transported antighost constructed below.
By Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:topologization}},
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cW)$ carries an
$\Ethree$-topological structure independent of the complex
structure of~$X$.

In particular, this applies to:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item the Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra
 $\cW_3^{(2)} = \cW^k(\mathfrak{sl}_3, f_{\min})$
 \textup{(}subregular/minimal nilpotent in
 $\mathfrak{sl}_3$\textup{)};
\item subregular $\cW$-algebras
 $\cW^k(\fg, f_{\mathrm{subreg}})$ for all simple~$\fg$;
\item hook-type $\cW$-algebras
 $\cW^k(\mathfrak{sl}_N, f_\lambda)$ for
 $\lambda = (N{-}r, 1^r)$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The argument reduces to Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}
by a single observation: the improvement term~$T_{\mathrm{imp}}(f)$
involves only \emph{Cartan currents}, regardless of the
nilpotent~$f$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~1: The $3$d bulk is independent of $f$.}
The Costello--Gaiotto theorem~\cite{costello-gaiotto} provides
$\cW^k(\fg, f)$ as the boundary chiral algebra of holomorphic
Chern--Simons for~$\fg$ at level~$k$ with DS boundary conditions
determined by~$f$. The bulk theory is the \emph{same} holomorphic
Chern--Simons for~$\fg$, independent of the nilpotent: the DS
reduction modifies the boundary condition, not the bulk BV-BRST
differential $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$. In particular, the identity
\begin{equation}\label{eq:current-Q-exact-general}
J_a \;=\; [Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, \bar c_a]\qquad
\text{on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology}
\end{equation}
holds for \emph{all} $a \in \fg$, by the same argument as
in~\eqref{eq:current-Q-exact}. This is a property of the
$3$d bulk, not the boundary.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~2: The improvement term for good-graded nilpotent data.}
The DS stress tensor for the good-graded nilpotent datum~$(f,x_0)$
decomposes as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:T-DS-general-decomp}
T_{\mathrm{DS}}(f) \;=\; T_{\mathrm{Sug}}
 \;+\; T_{\mathrm{imp}}(f),
\end{equation}
The ghost stress tensor $T_{\mathrm{ghost}}$ of the DS $(b,c)$-system,
when identified with bulk fields via the Costello--Gaiotto boundary
condition, is $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact by the same mechanism: each ghost
bilinear $:b_\alpha \partial c^\alpha:$ maps to a commutator
$[Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, (\text{bulk antighost})]$.
Here $T_{\mathrm{Sug}} = \frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}\sum_a
{:}J^a J_a{:}$ is the Sugawara stress tensor of~$V_k(\fg)$
and the improvement term is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:T-imp-general}
T_{\mathrm{imp}}(f) \;=\;
 +\sum_{i,j=1}^{\mathrm{rk}\,\fg}
 (x_0)_i\,
 (\kappa^{-1})^{h_i h_j}\,\partial J_{h_j},
\end{equation}
with $x_0 \in \fh$ the conformal grading
element\footnote{%
For the principal nilpotent,
$x_0 = \tfrac{1}{2}h_0 = \rho^{\vee}$ (the dual Weyl vector),
recovering the formula~\eqref{eq:T-imp-formula} of
Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}. For the minimal nilpotent
$f_{\min}$ in $\mathfrak{sl}_3$ with $h_0 = h_1$,
one has $x_0 = \tfrac{1}{2}h_1$ and the improvement reduces to
$T_{\mathrm{imp}} = \tfrac{1}{2}(\kappa^{-1})^{h_1 h_j}\,
\partial J_{h_j}$.}
and $(x_0)_i := \kappa(x_0, h_i)$ are the components of~$x_0$
in the chosen Cartan basis. The Cartan hypothesis is part of the
good-graded DS datum: after choosing the DS boundary condition, the
grading element defining the improved Virasoro vector lies in the
Cartan subalgebra used for the affine currents.

The ghost stress tensor $T_{\mathrm{ghost}}$ of the DS $(b,c)$-system, when identified with 3d bulk fields via the Costello--Gaiotto boundary condition, is $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact by the same mechanism: each ghost bilinear $:b_\alpha \partial c^\alpha:$ maps to a commutator $[Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, (\text{bulk antighost})]$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~3: Each summand is $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact.}

\emph{The Sugawara term.}
$[Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G_{\mathrm{Sug}}] = T_{\mathrm{Sug}}$
on cohomology, by the same argument as
in Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}. This step involves
no property of~$f$.

\emph{The improvement term.}
Since $x_0 \in \fh$, the improvement~\eqref{eq:T-imp-general}
involves only Cartan currents $\partial J_{h_j}$.
By~\eqref{eq:current-Q-exact-general}, each
$J_{h_j} = [Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, \bar c_{h_j}]$ on cohomology.
Since $\partial$ commutes with~$Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dJ-Q-exact-general}
\partial J_{h_j} \;=\;
\bigl[Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\,\partial\bar c_{h_j}\bigr].
\end{equation}

\emph{The DS-transported antighost.}
Define
\begin{equation}\label{eq:G-prime-general}
\boxed{\;
G'_f(z) \;:=\; G_{\mathrm{Sug}}(z)
 \;-\;
 \sum_{i,j=1}^{\mathrm{rk}\,\fg}
 (x_0)_i\,(\kappa^{-1})^{h_i h_j}\,
 \partial\bar c_{h_j}(z).
\;}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
[Q_{\mathrm{CS}},\, G'_f]
\;=\; T_{\mathrm{Sug}} + T_{\mathrm{imp}}(f)
\;=\; T_{\mathrm{DS}}(f)
\]
on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology. This
establishes~\eqref{eq:T-DS-BRST-general}.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Step~4: Topologization.}
Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} applies:
$T_{\mathrm{DS}}(f) = [Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G'_f]$ ensures
holomorphic translations are $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-exact, making
the factorisation algebra on the $\C$-direction locally constant
on cohomology, hence $\Etwo^{\mathrm{top}}$. Combined with the
$\Eone^{\mathrm{top}}$ from the transverse $\R$-direction,
Dunn additivity gives
$\Ethree^{\mathrm{top}}$ on
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cW^k(\fg, f))$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the non-principal obstructions are illusory
 for topologization]
\label{rem:non-principal-obstructions-illusory}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!non-principal!obstructions resolved}
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:bp-EN-level}} listed two qualitative
differences between the principal and non-principal DS reductions:
\textup{(1)}~the DS-BRST complex at a non-principal nilpotent
is non-Koszul \textup{(}irregular constraint system\textup{)},
and \textup{(2)}~the residual Levi factor can be non-abelian.
Neither obstructs topologization, for the following reasons.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Non-Koszulness.} The non-Koszulness of the DS complex
$C^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{DS}}(\fg, f)$ affects the computation
of $H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}$ and the presentation of~$\cW$ as a
vertex algebra \textup{(}e.g., the BRST cohomology can have
higher-cohomology contributions, and the generators of~$\cW$
may not be read off from the $E_1$-page of the Kazhdan
spectral sequence\textup{)}. But the topologization argument
operates entirely in the $3$d \emph{bulk} BV complex, where
the differential is the holomorphic CS
differential~$Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$ for~$\fg$.
The identity
$J_a = [Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, \bar c_a]$ is a property of the
$3$d bulk and is insensitive to the boundary DS complex.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Non-abelian Levi.} The non-abelian Levi factor
\textup{(}e.g., the residual $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ for the
Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra\textup{)} affects the representation
theory of~$\cW$ and the structure of the shadow obstruction
tower \textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:BP-shadow}}\textup{)}.
For topologization, however, the only datum that matters is the
improvement term $T_{\mathrm{imp}}(f)$, which is a linear
combination of \emph{Cartan current} derivatives
$\partial J_{h_j}$, determined by $x_0 = \tfrac{1}{2}h_0$,
a Cartan element regardless of the nilpotent orbit. The
non-abelian generators of the Levi contribute to the
$\cW$-algebra through the $G^\pm$ fields and their OPEs,
but they do not enter $T_{\mathrm{imp}}(f)$ and therefore
do not affect the BRST identity~\eqref{eq:T-DS-BRST-general}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Specialisation to Bershadsky--Polyakov]
\label{rem:E3-DS-BP-specialisation}
\index{Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra!DS-transported antighost}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_3$, $f = f_{\min}$ with
$h_0 = h_1 = \mathrm{diag}(1, -1, 0)$,
$h^\vee = 3$, $x_0 = \tfrac{1}{2}h_1$, and
$(\kappa^{-1})^{h_1 h_j}$ from the $\mathfrak{sl}_3$
Killing form, the DS-transported antighost
\eqref{eq:G-prime-general} reduces to
\[
G'_{f_{\min}}(z) \;=\;
\frac{1}{2(k+3)}\sum_{a \in \mathfrak{sl}_3}
{:}J^a(z)\,\bar c_a(z){:}
\;-\; \tfrac{1}{2}\sum_j
(\kappa^{-1})^{h_1 h_j}\,\partial\bar c_{h_j}(z).
\]
The BRST identity
$[Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G'_{f_{\min}}] = T_{\mathrm{BP}}$
holds on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology, giving
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cW_3^{(2)})$ an
$\Ethree$-topological structure.

Compare with the principal $\mathfrak{sl}_3$ case
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}}\textup{)}:
there $x_0 = \rho^\vee = \mathrm{diag}(1, 0, -1)$, and
the improvement correction involves \emph{both} Cartan
antighosts $\partial\bar c_{h_1}$ and~$\partial\bar c_{h_2}$.
For BP, $x_0 = \tfrac{1}{2}h_1 = \tfrac{1}{2}\mathrm{diag}(1,-1,0)$:
the correction involves only the $h_1$-component, reflecting
the fact that the minimal nilpotent constrains fewer directions
than the principal nilpotent.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[$\Ethree$-topological for quantized freely generated PVAs; \ClaimStatusConditional]\label{thm:E3-topological-free-PVA}
Let $\cA$ be a conformal vertex algebra at non-critical level
whose Li-filtration associated graded $\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{Li}}(\cA)$
is a finite-type freely generated Poisson vertex algebra with
finite-jet polynomial $\lambda$-bracket and inner holomorphic
translation. Assume the filtered boundary vertex algebra produced by
Theorem~\ref{thm:general-half-space-bv} is identified with~\(\cA\),
and assume that the conformal vector lifts to the quantized BV--BRST
complex with $T=[Q_{\mathrm{tot}},G]$.
Then $\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ carries an
$\Ethree$-topological algebra structure independent of the complex
structure of~$X$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Khan--Zeng construction~\cite{KZ25} attaches to a freely
generated PVA a classical three-dimensional Poisson-vertex sigma model
on $X \times \R$. The conformal vector upgrades the
holomorphic-topological symmetry to the classical topological symmetry
of \cite[Theorem~4.1]{KZ25}. The all-loop half-space BV quantization
is Theorem~\ref{thm:general-half-space-bv}, conditional on its KZ
analytic SDR package: the BV fields are constructed from the PVA
Hamiltonian bidifferential, and the reflected graph weights and QME
counterterms are supplied by that package.
The boundary identification supplies the boundary vertex algebra
\(\cA\). The assumed lift $T=[Q_{\mathrm{tot}},G]$ is exactly the
input required by Construction~\ref{constr:topologization}; applying
that construction to the quantized bulk gives the
$\Ethree$-topological structure.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-free-PVA}]
\label{rem:E3-top-free-PVA-scope}
The free-generation hypothesis on $\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{Li}}(\cA)$
is a genuine restriction. It applies on the original complex to the
families whose Li-graded Poisson vertex algebra is freely generated,
including the free-PVA and abelian/lattice cases and the relevant
non-critical affine specialisations. It does not assert a generic
original-complex theorem for class~M. The class~M statement lives in
the weight-completed/pro ambient of
Corollary~\ref*{cor:universal-holography-class-M}, with the strict
original-complex $E_3$ lift only in the conditional scope recorded
there.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[$\Ethree$-topological for general conformal chiral algebras; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:E3-topological-general}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!general conjecture|textbf}
\index{derived center!E3 topologization@$\Ethree$ topologization}
\index{conformal vector!general topologization conjecture}
Let $A$ be a chiral algebra with conformal vector $T(z)$ at
non-critical level. Suppose $A$ arises as the boundary of a
$3$d holomorphic-topological theory on $X \times \R$
\textup{(}that is, input~\textup{\ref{item:E3-existence}} of
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:E3-topological-separation}} is
satisfied\textup{)}. Then the BV-BRST complex of the $3$d bulk
admits a field~$G(z)$ satisfying $T(z) = [Q, G(z)]$, and
Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:topologization}} gives
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$ an $\Ethree$-topological structure
independent of the complex structure of~$X$.

At critical level $k = -h^{\vee}$, the conformal vector
degenerates and topologization fails: $\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$
remains $\Ethree$-chiral but not $\Ethree$-topological. When
the conformal vector is absent entirely, the derived center
carries only the $\SCchtop$ structure, and the $\Etwo$ factor
remains chiral rather than topological.
By Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-free-PVA}, this conjecture holds on
the KZ finite-type freely generated locus only under the KZ analytic SDR
package and the quantized topological lift. By
Theorem~\ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3} it holds for the Moonshine
module~$V^\natural$ via the Leech lattice orbifold route. The remaining
frontier consists of non-freely-generated conformal vertex algebras
without an orbifold or coset presentation from a parent with the needed
quantization, topological lift, and vanishing anomaly data; no example
from the standard landscape is currently known to fall in this frontier
case.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{theorem}[$\Ethree$-topological for the Monster VOA $V^\natural$ via orbifold route; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:monster-orbifold-e3}
\index{Monster VOA!E3-topological via orbifold route|textbf}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!Monster VOA}
\index{Moonshine module!E3-topological}
\index{Dijkgraaf--Witten class!Leech lattice vanishing}
The derived chiral center $\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^\natural)$
of the Moonshine module
$V^\natural = V_\Lambda \,/\!/\, \Z/2$ carries an
$\Ethree$-topological algebra structure.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Moonshine module decomposes as
$V^\natural = V_\Lambda^+ \oplus V_\Lambda^{\mathrm{tw},+}$,
the untwisted and twisted $\Z/2$-invariant sectors of the
Leech lattice VOA~$V_\Lambda$ under the lift of
$\sigma\colon \alpha \mapsto -\alpha$
\cite{FLM88}. We prove $\Ethree$-topologicality in four
steps.

\emph{Step 1 (parent is $\Ethree$-topological).} The Leech
lattice VOA $V_\Lambda$ has Li-filtration associated graded
the free Poisson vertex algebra on $24$ generators of weight
one (Heisenberg currents $J^i$) twisted by the Leech lattice
theta. It is therefore covered by
Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-free-PVA}; concretely, the
$3$d HT bulk is abelian holomorphic Chern--Simons for the
rank-$24$ torus $U(1)^{24}$ with Leech lattice charge lattice,
quantised by Costello--Li~\cite{CostelloLi2020}. The Sugawara
conformal vector $T = \tfrac{1}{2}\sum {:}J^i J_i{:}$ and the
corresponding antighost $G = \tfrac{1}{2}\sum {:}J^i \bar c_i{:}$
satisfy $T = [Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G]$ on $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$-cohomology.

\emph{Step 2 ($\Z/2$-equivariance of the bulk BV data).}
The Leech involution $\sigma\colon J^i \mapsto -J^i$ lifts
canonically to the BV antifields $\bar c_i \mapsto -\bar c_i$
and to the rank-$24$ abelian holomorphic CS action
$S = \tfrac{1}{2}\int A^i \wedge \bar\partial A_i$, which is
$\sigma$-invariant because $A^i A_i$ is bilinear. Hence
$\sigma$ acts on the factorisation algebra of observables
$\mathrm{Obs}(V_\Lambda)$ of Costello--Li, and the
\emph{entire} BV data $(Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, S, T, G)$ is
$\sigma$-equivariant since each object is a $\sigma$-invariant
quadratic expression in the fields.

\emph{Step 3 (Dijkgraaf--Witten anomaly vanishes).} The
obstruction to gauging the $\Z/2$-symmetry of rank-$24$
abelian holomorphic CS is the Dijkgraaf--Witten class
$\alpha_\sigma \in H^3(B\Z/2, U(1)) \cong \Z/2$
\cite{DW90}, represented by the Arf invariant of the
quadratic refinement of the Leech bilinear form restricted
to the $\sigma$-fixed sublattice. Since $\sigma=-1$ and
$\Lambda$ is torsion-free, the $+1$-eigenspace of~$\sigma$
contains only the origin; the restricted form is therefore the
trivial quadratic form on the trivial lattice, whose Arf
invariant is zero. Equivalently, the Monster partition
function
$Z_{V^\natural}(\tau) = J(\tau) = j(\tau) - 744$
is $\SL_2(\Z)$-invariant~\cite{Borcherds92}, which is the
operational witness of anomaly vanishing via the
$T$-modular action on orbifold sectors (FLM$88$,
Dijkgraaf--Vafa--Verlinde--Verlinde
$1989$). Therefore the $\Z/2$-gauged abelian holomorphic CS
theory exists.

\emph{Step 4 (orbifold BV and boundary identification).}
The $\Z/2$-gauged BV complex decomposes as
$\mathcal F^{\mathrm{orb}} =
\mathcal F^{\Z/2\text{-inv}} \oplus
\mathcal F^{\Z/2\text{-tw}}$, with the invariant sector
equal to the $\sigma$-fixed part of the Costello--Li
factorisation algebra and the twisted sector built from
fields with $\sigma$-anti-periodic boundary conditions
around the $\Z/2$-holonomy. Because the action is quadratic
and $\sigma$-invariant, the BV master equation
$\{S^{\mathrm{orb}}, S^{\mathrm{orb}}\} = 0$ reduces
sector by sector to the ungauged master equation on
$\sigma$-invariant fields; Step~$3$ eliminates the
obstruction to coherent gluing of the two sectors. The
boundary factorisation algebra of $\mathcal F^{\mathrm{orb}}$
on $X \times \{0\}$ is precisely the orbifold VOA
$V_\Lambda^{\mathrm{orb}} = V_\Lambda^+ \oplus
V_\Lambda^{\mathrm{tw},+} = V^\natural$
\cite{Huang2015, DijkgraafVafaVerlindeVerlinde1989}.
Finally, $Q_{\mathrm{CS}}$, $T$, and $G$ are all
$\sigma$-invariant by Step~$2$, hence descend to the
$\Z/2$-gauged bulk as $(Q^{\mathrm{orb}}, T, G^{\mathrm{orb}})$
satisfying $T = [Q^{\mathrm{orb}}, G^{\mathrm{orb}}]$ on
$Q^{\mathrm{orb}}$-cohomology. Construction~\ref{constr:topologization}
applied to the orbifold bulk produces the
$\Ethree$-topological structure on
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^\natural)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope after Theorem~\ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3}]
\label{rem:monster-orbifold-route}
\index{Monster VOA!orbifold route to E3-topological}
Theorem~\ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3} gives the Moonshine module by a
special Leech $\Z/2$ finite-orbifold descent. It is not a generic
class-$M$ original-complex theorem. For the holomorphic $c=24$
Schellekens surface, the separate three-stratum theorem
\ref{thm:schellekens-71-all-alpha-zero} computes the relevant
Dijkgraaf--Witten classes; the Monster is the Type~B case. The
remaining frontier of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:E3-topological-general} is therefore
case~\ref{item:scope-frontier} of
Remark~\ref{rem:e3-topological-scope-map}: non-freely
generated conformal vertex algebras admitting neither an
orbifold nor coset presentation from a freely generated
parent.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[$T$-duality and lattice orbifolds for lattice vertex algebras]
\label{rem:t-duality-lattice-voa}
\index{T-duality!lattice vertex algebras}
\index{lattice vertex algebra!T-duality}
\index{orbifold!T-dual presentation}
The Monster construction above fits a general
$T$-duality/orbifold compatibility at the level of
$\Eone$-chiral structure on lattice vertex
algebras~\cite{FLM88,Borcherds92}. Let
$L \subset \R^n$ be a rank-$n$ even lattice with dual
lattice $L^* = \{\,v \in \R^n : \langle v, \ell \rangle \in \Z
\text{ for all } \ell \in L\,\}$. The lattice vertex algebra
$V_L$ is $T$-dual to $V_{L^*}$: the inversion
$z \leftrightarrow 1/z$ on the spectral-parameter space of
the Heisenberg currents $\alpha^i(z)$ interchanges momentum
and winding sublattices, and the resulting map
$V_L \to V_{L^*}$ is an equivalence of
$\Eone$-chiral algebras at the bar-complex level (on bar
degree $1$, it is the lattice-level automorphism
$\alpha \mapsto \alpha^*$ coupled with $z \mapsto 1/z$; on
higher bar degrees it is extended by the corresponding
involution of the collision operad). For self-dual
unimodular lattices $L = L^*$ the $T$-duality is an
involution of $V_L$; for non-self-dual $L$, $T$-duality
identifies the $\Eone$-chiral datum of $V_L$ with that of a
genuinely distinct lattice vertex algebra $V_{L^*}$.

The construction orbifolds: for any subgroup
$G \subset \Aut(L)$ preserving the bilinear form, the
$G$-invariant subalgebra $V_L^G$ is $\Eone$-chiral (it
inherits the bar complex of $V_L$ under exact
$G$-coinvariants), and its $T$-dual is $V_{L^*}^{G^*}$ where
$G^*$ is the Pontryagin dual of $G$ acting on $L^*$. Taking
$G = \Z/2$ acting by $\ell \mapsto -\ell$ yields the
orbifold presentation $V_L^{+} \oplus V_L^{\mathrm{tw},+}$
used in Theorem~\ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3}. The Leech
lattice $\Lambda$ is even unimodular
($\Lambda = \Lambda^*$), so $T$-duality acts as the identity
on the diagonal and the Monster module
$V^\natural = V_\Lambda \,/\!/\, \Z/2$ is a fixed point of
the combined $T$-duality plus lattice-orbifold operation.
This places the $\Ethree$-topological structure on
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^\natural)$ inside a broader family:
every even unimodular lattice produces a $T$-duality fixed
point, and the same four-step proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3} applies to the Fake
Monster (via the Lorentzian lattice $II_{25,1}$) and to each
of the $24$ Niemeier lattices whose Dijkgraaf--Witten
obstruction vanishes. The $T$-duality/orbifold square
commutes with the chiral derived-center functor
$\Zder^{\mathrm{ch}}$, so the holography established in
Theorem~\ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3} is covariant under
this group of equivalences.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Which chiral algebras admit a $3$d HT bulk?]
\label{rem:E3-existence-landscape}
\index{E3-chiral algebra@$\Ethree$-chiral algebra!existence landscape}
\index{Feigin--Frenkel center!critical level obstruction}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:E3-topological-general} presupposes the
existence of a $3$d HT theory with boundary~$A$.
For gauge-theoretic families this is known:
affine Kac--Moody via holomorphic
Chern--Simons~\cite{CostelloLi2020}, and $\cW$-algebras
via Costello--Gaiotto (holomorphic CS with DS boundary
conditions). For chiral algebras without gauge-theoretic
origin (lattice VOAs with non-abelian structure,
Calabi--Yau functor outputs, exceptional $\cW$-algebras not
obtainable by DS), a direct construction
(e.g.\ quantising the Poisson vertex model) is required and
remains open.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope map for $\Ethree$-topological topologization]
\label{rem:e3-topological-scope-map}
\index{E3-topological algebra@$\Ethree$-topological algebra!scope map}
We collect, in one place, the precise status of the
$\Ethree$-topological upgrade as a function of the input data.
``Freely generated'' here means that the Li-filtration associated
graded $\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{Li}}(\cA)$ is a polynomial PVA in
finitely many strong generators of prescribed conformal weights;
this is the Khan--Zeng hypothesis~\cite[\S 3]{KZ25} and it is
stable under tensor product and finite \'etale base change but
\emph{not} under orbifold by a non-trivial finite group action.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]
\item\label{item:scope-free-noncrit}
  \emph{Freely generated $+$ conformal vector at non-critical level.}
  $\Ethree$-topological is proved in the affine and DS sublanes
  \textup{(}Theorems~\ref{thm:E3-topological-km},
  \ref{thm:E3-topological-DS},
  \ref{thm:E3-topological-DS-general}\textup{)} and conditional on the
  KZ analytic SDR package plus the quantized topological lift in the
  general finite-type freely generated PVA lane
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-free-PVA}\textup{)} via Costello--Li
  holomorphic Chern--Simons, Costello--Gaiotto holomorphic CS with
  DS boundary, and Khan--Zeng PV sigma model, respectively.
  Covers affine Kac--Moody $V_k(\fg)$, Virasoro $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ at
  $c \neq 26$, all $\cW_N$ with any good nilpotent, Bershadsky--Polyakov,
  Heisenberg $H_k$ $(k \neq 0)$, and lattice VOAs $V_L$ for even positive
  definite $L$.
\item\label{item:scope-free-crit}
  \emph{Freely generated $+$ critical level
  $k = -h^{\vee}$.}
  Sugawara element degenerates; no inner conformal vector
  in $Q$-cohomology. Topologization \emph{fails}; the derived
  center remains $\Ethree$-chiral and collapses to the
  Feigin--Frenkel center at cohomology.
\item\label{item:scope-orbifold}
  \emph{Non-freely-generated but obtained as finite group orbifold or
  coset from a freely-generated parent with vanishing
  anomaly.} $\Ethree$-topological \emph{proved by inheritance}
  when (a)~the parent is covered by case~\ref{item:scope-free-noncrit};
  (b)~the conformal vector and the antighost~$G(z)$ are invariant
  under the finite group or coset projection; and (c)~the
  Dijkgraaf--Witten class in $H^3(BG, U(1))$ (orbifold) or the
  coset anomaly (coset) vanishes. Under (a)--(c), factorisation
  $\Ethree$-structure descends because finite group invariants and
  commutants preserve $E_n$-structure at the level of factorisation
  algebras \textup{(}Costello--Gwilliam~\cite{CG17}, Vol.~I
  \S 5\textup{)}.
  Covers the invariant subalgebra $V_\Lambda^+$ of the Leech lattice
  VOA (see Remark~\ref{rem:monster-orbifold-route});
  covers parafermion algebras $K(\fg,k)$ as the coset of $V_k(\fg)$
  by its Heisenberg subalgebra. The full Moonshine module
  $V^\natural = V_\Lambda \,/\!/\, \Z/2$
  (twisted-sector orbifold) is covered by
  Theorem~\ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3}: the $\Z/2$-gauged
  abelian holomorphic CS theory exists because the
  Dijkgraaf--Witten class
  $\alpha \in H^3(B\Z/2, U(1))$ vanishes, forced by the
  even unimodularity of the Leech lattice and equivalently
  witnessed by $\SL_2(\Z)$-invariance of the Monster
  partition function~$J(\tau)$.
\item\label{item:scope-frontier}
  \emph{Non-freely-generated without orbifold or coset parent.}
  The genuine frontier. No example in the standard landscape is
  currently known to fall here. Candidate settings considered
  (exceptional $\cW$-algebras outside DS, non-unitary logarithmic
  triplet algebras $\cW(p)$ at $p \geq 2$, Calabi--Yau functor
  outputs in Vol.~III) each either (i)~admit an orbifold or coset
  presentation from a freely-generated parent and fall under
  case~\ref{item:scope-orbifold}, or (ii)~lack a conformal vector
  at non-critical level and therefore fall outside the hypothesis
  of Conjecture~\ref{conj:E3-topological-general}.
  If no member of the standard landscape populates
  case~\ref{item:scope-frontier}, then
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:E3-topological-general} is vacuously a
  theorem \emph{on the standard landscape}. Whether a genuine
  witness to case~\ref{item:scope-frontier} exists is itself a
  well-posed open problem.
\end{enumerate}
The previous phrasing in
Remark~\ref{rem:E3-top-free-PVA-scope} asserting that ``every
conformal vertex algebra in the $G/L/C/M$ classification at
non-critical level'' is freely generated is correct as a
statement about the standard landscape but should not be read as
a universal quantifier over all conformal chiral algebras: the
Moonshine module, cosets $K(\fg,k)$, and the logarithmic triplet
$\cW(p)$ all fall into case~\ref{item:scope-orbifold} rather
than~\ref{item:scope-free-noncrit}. The present remark is the
canonical scope statement; downstream citations should point
here when discussing the generality of the topologization
climax.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The $\Ethree$ dichotomy and the volume's architecture]
\label{rem:E3-dichotomy-architecture}
\index{E3-algebra@$\Ethree$-algebra!dichotomy}
The passage from $\Ethree$-chiral to $\Ethree$-topological is
the volume's climax. For affine Kac--Moody at non-critical
level, this passage is a theorem
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-km}\textup{)}.
For $\cW$-algebras obtained by \emph{any} DS reduction,
whether principal
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS}\textup{)} or
non-principal
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-DS-general}\textup{)},
including Virasoro, all $\cW_N$, and the Bershadsky--Polyakov
algebra, it is also a theorem:
the Costello--Gaiotto theorem provides the $3$d HT theory,
and the BRST identity
$T_{\mathrm{DS}} = [Q_{\mathrm{CS}}, G'_f]$ is verified by
constructing the DS-transported antighost~$G'_f$ from the
Sugawara antighost plus an improvement correction built from
derivatives of the $3$d BV antighosts.
Construction~\ref{constr:topologization} shows that the
topologization mechanism is cohomological: whenever a $3$d HT
bulk carries $T=[Q,G]$, the conformal vector topologizes the
$\Etwo$-chiral factor on $Q$-cohomology. The resulting
  $\Ethree$-topological structure is proved in the affine, DS, and
  orbifold lanes
  \textup{(}Theorems~\ref{thm:E3-topological-km},
  \ref{thm:E3-topological-DS},
  \ref{thm:E3-topological-DS-general},
  \ref{thm:monster-orbifold-e3}\textup{)}; a general
  finite-type KZ freely-generated-PVA lane is conditional on
  Theorem~\ref{thm:E3-topological-free-PVA}; a general chain-level
  lift outside these lanes remains conjectural
\textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:E3-topological-general}\textup{)}.
Without the conformal vector, the bulk depends on the complex
structure of~$X$ and one has a holomorphic-topological theory
rather than a TQFT.
\end{remark}

%====================================================================
% THE EXPLICIT GENUS-1 MAURER--CARTAN DATUM
%====================================================================

\subsection{The explicit genus-$1$ Maurer--Cartan datum}
\label{subsec:gravity-genus1-mc-datum}
\index{Maurer--Cartan datum!genus-1|textbf}
\index{modular bar complex!genus-1}
\index{Dedekind eta function!from bar complex}

Movements I--V derived the genus tower from the $\hat A$-genus
formula. This section computes the genus-$1$ bar complex
$\barB^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ from first principles: the
explicit modular Maurer--Cartan element $\Theta^{(1)}$, its
trace recovering $F_1 = c/48$, the $n$-point genus-$1$
amplitudes, and the genus-$1$ correction to the spectral
$R$-matrix. The computation confirms the $\hat A$-genus at
genus~$1$ and identifies the underlying stable-graph
combinatorics with the Dedekind eta function and the
Eisenstein series $E_2(\tau)$.

\subsubsection*{The genus-$1$ bar complex}

The genus-$1$ bar complex
$\barB^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ is the component of the
modular bar coalgebra (Definition~\ref{def:complete-modular-bar})
at total genus~$1$. There is a single genus-$1$ stable graph
type at each degree~$n$: a corolla with $n$ external legs, one
vertex of genus~$0$, and \emph{one internal self-loop}.
Write $\Gamma_{1,n}$ for this graph. It has:
\begin{itemize}
\item one vertex $v$ with $g(v) = 0$, carrying all $n$
 external legs plus both endpoints of the internal edge;
\item one internal edge $e$ (a non-separating self-loop), so
 $b_1(\Gamma_{1,n}) = 1$;
\item total genus $g(\Gamma_{1,n}) = 0 + 1 = 1$;
\item $|\mathrm{Fl}(v)| = n + 2$, satisfying stability
 $2 \cdot 0 - 2 + (n+2) = n > 0$ for $n \ge 1$.
\end{itemize}

As a vector space at degree $n$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-bar-degree}
\barB^{(1)}_n(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\;\cong\;
\orline(\Gamma_{1,n})
\;\otimes\;
(s^{-1}\mathrm{Vir}_c)^{\otimes n},
\end{equation}
where the orientation line $\orline(\Gamma_{1,n})
= \det(k\{e\}) \otimes \det(H_1(\Gamma_{1,n};k))^{-1}
\cong k$ is trivial (one edge, one loop: the determinants cancel).
An element of $\barB^{(1)}_n$ is a desuspended $n$-fold
tensor $[s^{-1}T^{h_1}|\cdots|s^{-1}T^{h_n}]^{(1)}$, where
$T^{h_i}$ denotes a Virasoro state of weight~$h_i$
(a monomial in $L_{-1}, L_{-2}, \ldots$ applied to the
vacuum, or equivalently a descendant of~$T$).

\subsubsection*{The curved differential at genus $1$}

The total differential on $\barB^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ has
two components:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-diff-decomp}
D^{(1)} \;=\; D_0^{(1)} + D_1,
\end{equation}
where $D_0^{(1)}$ is the genus-preserving part (the genus-$0$
bar differential restricted to genus-$1$ graphs) and
$D_1 = D_{\mathrm{nsep}}$ is the non-separating one-edge
expansion that raises genus by~$1$ (applied to genus-$0$
bar elements to produce genus-$1$ elements).

The key identity is the \emph{curved} relation at genus~$1$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-curvature}
(D_0^{(1)})^2 \;=\; \kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \omega_1
\;=\; \frac{c}{2}\,\omega_1,
\end{equation}
where $\omega_1 \in H^{1,1}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1})$
is the first Hodge class, and the identity holds on the fibre over
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$.

\begin{remark}[The curvature is intrinsic, not effective]
\label{rem:genus1-intrinsic-curvature}
The curvature in~\eqref{eq:genus1-curvature} is
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$, the \emph{intrinsic} modular
characteristic. The effective curvature
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/2$ arises only after coupling to
ghosts (Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-kappa-vs-kappa-eff}).
The algebraic bar complex sees $\kappa = c/2$; the physical
partition function uses $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/2$.
\end{remark}

\begin{computation}[Explicit genus-$1$ fibre differential for $T \otimes T$;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:genus1-fibre-diff-TT}%
\index{fibre differential!genus-1 explicit formula|textbf}%
\index{Eisenstein series!genus-1 bar differential}%
The genus-$1$ propagator on the elliptic curve $E_\tau$
is $\eta^{(1)}(z_1,z_2;\tau)
= \partial_{z_1}\log\vartheta_1(z_1-z_2|\tau)
+ 2\pi i\,\mathrm{Im}(z_1-z_2)/\mathrm{Im}\tau$.
Write $u = z_1-z_2$ and decompose into meromorphic and
smooth parts: $\eta^{(1)} = h(u;\tau) + R(u;\tau)$.
The Laurent expansion of the meromorphic part is
\[
h(u;\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{u}
- \frac{\pi^2}{3}\,E_2(\tau)\,u
- \frac{\pi^4}{45}\,E_4(\tau)\,u^3
- \cdots
\;=\;
\frac{1}{u}
+ \sum_{k=1}^{\infty} c_k(\tau)\,u^{2k-1},
\]
where $c_k(\tau) = (-1)^k\frac{(2\pi)^{2k}}{(2k)!}\,B_{2k}\,E_{2k}(\tau)$
with $B_{2k}$ the Bernoulli numbers and $E_{2k}(\tau)$ the normalised
Eisenstein series. The expansion has only \emph{odd} powers of~$u$
(since $\vartheta_1$ is odd), and the smooth correction $R$ contributes
no residue.

\emph{The three-term formula.}
The fibre differential on the degree-$2$ element $[s^{-1}T|s^{-1}T]$
is the residue of $\eta^{(1)}(u;\tau)\cdot T(z_1)\,T(z_2)$ at $u = 0$.
The Virasoro OPE
$T(z_1)\,T(z_2) \sim (c/2)/u^4 + 2T/u^2 + \partial T/u$
