has poles at orders $4$, $2$, and~$1$. Pairing with the propagator's
odd-power terms:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-dfib-TT}
\boxed{
d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{(1)}[s^{-1}T \,|\, s^{-1}T]
\;=\;
s^{-1}\Bigl(
 {:}TT{:}
 \;-\; \frac{2\pi^2}{3}\,E_2(\tau)\cdot T
 \;-\; \frac{c\pi^4}{90}\,E_4(\tau)\cdot \mathbf{1}
\Bigr).
}
\end{equation}
The three terms have distinct origins:
\begin{itemize}
\item ${:}TT{:}$: the normal-ordered product (genus-$0$ answer),
 from the leading propagator $1/u$ paired with the regular
 term ${:}TT{:}$ in the OPE;
\item $-\frac{2\pi^2}{3}\,E_2(\tau)\cdot T$: the genus-$1$
 state-dependent correction, from the double pole $2T/u^2$
 paired with the propagator coefficient $c_1(\tau)\,u
 = -\frac{\pi^2}{3}E_2(\tau)\,u$;
\item $-\frac{c\pi^4}{90}\,E_4(\tau)\cdot\mathbf{1}$: the
 genus-$1$ vacuum (contact) correction, from the quartic pole
 $(c/2)/u^4$ paired with $c_2(\tau)\,u^3
 = -\frac{\pi^4}{45}E_4(\tau)\,u^3$.
\end{itemize}
The $E_2$-correction is quasi-modular; the $E_4$-correction is modular.
Each OPE pole of order~$2k$ generates a genus-$1$ shadow weighted by
the Eisenstein series~$E_{2k}(\tau)$.

\emph{General weight formula.}
For states $a, b$ of conformal weights $h_a, h_b$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-dfib-general}
d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{(1)}[s^{-1}a \,|\, s^{-1}b]
\;=\;
s^{-1}\Bigl(
 a_{(-1)}b
 \;+\;
 \sum_{k=1}^{\lfloor (h_a+h_b)/2\rfloor}
 c_k(\tau)\cdot a_{(2k-1)}b
\Bigr),
\end{equation}
where $a_{(-1)}b = {:}ab{:}$ is the normal-ordered product and
the sum runs over odd OPE products $a_{(2k-1)}b$ weighted by the
propagator coefficients $c_k(\tau)$. The sum terminates because
the OPE has finitely many singular terms.
\end{computation}

\begin{proof}
The fibre differential at genus~$1$ is defined by
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{(1)}[s^{-1}a|s^{-1}b]
= s^{-1}\operatorname{Res}_{z_1=z_2}[
\eta^{(1)}(z_1,z_2;\tau)\cdot a(z_1)\,b(z_2)]$.
The smooth correction $R(u;\tau)$ vanishes at $u = 0$ and
contributes no residue. The meromorphic part
$h(u;\tau) = 1/u + \sum_{k \ge 1}c_k(\tau)\,u^{2k-1}$
multiplied by the OPE
$a(z_1)\,b(z_2) = \sum_{n \ge 0}a_{(n)}b\cdot u^{-(n+1)}
+ {:}ab{:} + O(u)$
has residue
$\operatorname{Res}_{u=0}[h\cdot\mathrm{OPE}]
= a_{(-1)}b + \sum_{k}c_k\cdot a_{(2k-1)}b$,
where the cross-terms $c_k\,u^{2k-1}\cdot a_{(n)}b\,u^{-(n+1)}$
contribute to the residue precisely when $n = 2k-1$.
For $a = b = T$: the non-zero products are $T_{(1)}T = 2T$
(giving $c_1\cdot 2T$) and $T_{(3)}T = c/2$ (giving
$c_2\cdot c/2$), which yield the three-term
formula~\eqref{eq:gravity-dfib-TT}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The genus-$1$ Maurer--Cartan element}

By the universal genus-$1$ obstruction theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:Ob1}), the genus-$1$ MC element
$\Theta^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$ exists if and only if the
genus-$1$ obstruction class
$\mathrm{Ob}_1(\Theta_0) = [D_1 \Theta_0]$ vanishes in
$H^2(\mathrm{gr}_F^1 L_{\mathrm{mod}},\, d_0^{\Theta_0})$.
For the Virasoro, this class vanishes because the
cyclic Hochschild cohomology
$H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ is trivial in the
relevant degree (the Virasoro has a unique genus-$1$ extension
at each conformal weight, determined by $\kappa$).

\begin{theorem}[Explicit genus-$1$ MC element for Virasoro;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:genus1-mc-virasoro}
\index{Maurer--Cartan datum!explicit genus-1 MC element|textbf}
\index{universal MC element!genus-1!Virasoro}
The genus-$1$ component of the universal MC element is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-explicit}
\Theta^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}
\;=\;
\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}\,
\sum_{\Gamma \in \mathcal{G}_{1,n}}
\frac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)|}\;
w_\Gamma \cdot I_\Gamma,
\end{equation}
where the sum ranges over connected stable graphs $\Gamma$ of
genus~$1$ with $n$ external legs, $w_\Gamma$ is the weight form
on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,n}$, and $I_\Gamma$ is the
graph integral (vertex tensors contracted along edges using the
bar propagator).

At genus~$1$, every stable graph decomposes uniquely as a tree
of genus-$0$ vertices grafted onto a single loop (the
non-separating cycle). The loop carries the genus: it is an
internal edge whose two endpoints share the same vertex
(after collapsing the tree parts).

\emph{Degree $n = 0$ (the vacuum graph).}
The unique graph is the self-loop $\Gamma_{1,0}$: one vertex,
one self-loop, no external legs.
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-degree0}
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}
\;=\;
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \omega_1
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\omega_1,
\end{equation}
where the self-loop contracts the two flags of the internal
edge using the cyclic inner product
$\langle L_{-n}, L_m \rangle =
\frac{c}{12}(n^3-n)\,\delta_{n,m}$ and sums over modes:
\[
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}
\;=\;
\sum_{n=1}^{\infty}
\frac{c}{12}(n^3-n)\cdot q^n \cdot \omega_1
\;=\;
\kappa \cdot \omega_1
\]
(where the mode sum is absorbed into the definition of the
Hodge class; the numerical value $\kappa = c/2$ is the total
trace of the normalized propagator on the self-loop).

\emph{Degree $n = 1$ (the tadpole).}
One external leg, one self-loop. The vertex carries three
flags: the external leg plus the two endpoints of the
self-loop. The MC coefficient at degree~$1$ is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-degree1}
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=1}(T)
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24}\,T,
\end{equation}
because the self-loop contraction of $T(z)$ at genus~$1$ gives
\[
\oint_{A} \oint_{B}
\frac{T(w)}{(z-w)^2}\,\frac{dz\,dw}{2\pi i}
\;=\;
\sum_{n \ge 1} n \cdot q^n \cdot T
\;=\;
\frac{E_2(\tau)}{24}\cdot T,
\]
where $E_2(\tau) = 1 - 24\sum_{n \ge 1}\sigma_1(n)\,q^n$ is
the quasi-modular Eisenstein series of weight~$2$.
The leading term (constant in $q$) gives $-c/24$ times the
stress tensor, while the $q$-dependent corrections encode the
higher-degree genus-$1$ terms, the graviton-vertex corrections.

\begin{remark}[Casimir energy vs.\ free energy]
The degree-$1$ coefficient $-(c/24)\,T$ is the Casimir energy density,
not the scalar-lane free energy
$F_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = (c/2)\cdot(1/24) = c/48$ .
The factor $\kappa = c/2$ is the curvature of the Virasoro algebra;
$\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = 1/24$ is the Hodge integral
$\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}}\lambda_1$.
\end{remark}

More precisely, the genus-$1$ one-point function on a torus of
modular parameter~$\tau$ is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-one-point}
\langle T \rangle_{g=1}
\;=\;
\operatorname{tr}_{V_c}\!\left(L_0\,q^{L_0 - c/24}\right)\cdot
\bigl(\operatorname{tr}_{V_c} q^{L_0 - c/24}\bigr)^{-1}
\;=\;
\frac{q\,\partial_q \log Z_1(\tau)}{1}
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24} + O(q),
\end{equation}
confirming~\eqref{eq:genus1-mc-degree1} at leading order.

\emph{Degree $n = 2$ (the bubble).}
Two external legs, one self-loop. The MC coefficient encodes
the genus-$1$ two-point function:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-degree2}
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=2}(T,T;\,z_{12})
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\wp(z_{12};\tau)
\;+\;
2\,\langle T(z_1)T(z_2)\rangle_{g=1}^{\mathrm{conn}},
\end{equation}
where $\wp(z;\tau)$ is the Weierstrass $\wp$-function; the
Green's function on the torus is $\wp(z;\tau) + E_2(\tau)/12$.
The first term is the
genus-$1$ graviton exchange through the self-loop (the
$c$-dependent piece); the second is the matter
contribution.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The computation proceeds by the filtered obstruction theory of
Theorem~\ref{thm:Ob1}. The genus-$0$ MC element
$\Theta_0 = \Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}^{(0)}$ is the standard
bar element encoding the $\Ainf$ structure from Movement~I.
The genus-raising operator $D_1 = D_{\mathrm{nsep}}$ acts on
$\Theta_0$ by self-sewing: pairing two flags of a genus-$0$
corolla with the cyclic inner product, creating a self-loop.

\emph{Degree-$0$ computation.}
The self-sewing of the binary vertex $m_2$ gives the degree-$0$
genus-$1$ element. The cyclic trace of $m_2$ over a pair of
flags is:
\[
D_1(m_2)_{n=0}
\;=\;
\sum_{h} \langle e^h | m_2 | e_h \rangle
\;=\;
\mathrm{Tr}(L_0) \cdot \omega_1
\;=\;
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \omega_1,
\]
where $\{e_h\}$, $\{e^h\}$ are dual bases of $\mathrm{Vir}_c$
and the trace is the modular characteristic
$\kappa = c/2$.

\emph{Degree-$1$ computation.}
Self-sewing of the ternary vertex $m_3$ (from
Movement~I,~\eqref{eq:gravity-m3}) on two of its three legs
gives:
\[
D_1(m_3)_{n=1}(T)
\;=\;
\sum_{h} \langle e^h | m_3(e_h, T) \rangle
\;+\;
\sum_{h} \langle e^h | m_3(T, e_h) \rangle.
\]
By the explicit formula~\eqref{eq:gravity-m3} and the Virasoro
inner product, each sum evaluates to a trace over
$\mathrm{Vir}_c$-descendants. At weight~$h$, the contribution
involves the Kac determinant at level~$h$, and the total is:
\[
\sum_{n=1}^{\infty} p(n)\cdot n\cdot q^n \cdot T
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24}\,T + O(q),
\]
where $p(n)$ counts partitions (the number of states at
level~$n$). The leading coefficient $-c/24$ is the genus-$1$
free energy density.

\emph{Degree-$2$ computation.}
The self-sewing of $m_4$ and the composition $m_2 \circ m_2$
through the genus-$1$ propagator give:
\[
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=2}(T,T;\,z_{12})
\;=\;
\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}
\langle T(z_1) | q^{L_0-c/24} | T(z_2) \rangle
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\wp(z_{12};\tau) + E_2 \cdot T \otimes T + \cdots.
\]
The Weierstrass $\wp$-function arises as the genus-$1$ chiral
Green's function, which is the sum
$\wp(z;\tau) = \frac{1}{z^2} +
\sum_{(m,n) \ne (0,0)}
\bigl(\frac{1}{(z-m-n\tau)^2} - \frac{1}{(m+n\tau)^2}\bigr)$
(the doubly-periodic meromorphic function with a
second-order pole at the lattice points).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The trace: recovering $F_1 = \kappa/24 = c/48$}

\begin{computation}[Genus-$1$ free energy from the MC trace;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:genus1-free-energy}
\index{genus-1 free energy!from MC trace|textbf}
\index{Bernoulli number!$B_2 = 1/6$}
The genus-$1$ free energy is the trace of $\Theta^{(1)}$
over the genus-$1$ modular bar complex:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-trace}
F_1(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\;=\;
\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}\bigr)
\;=\;
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}},
\qquad \end{equation}
where $\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}}
= \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \lambda_1
= 1/24$ is the integral of the Hodge class over
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$.

\emph{Explicit evaluation.}
$F_1(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = (c/2) \cdot (1/24) = c/48$. This is the
\emph{intrinsic} genus-$1$ free energy, using the intrinsic
curvature $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$. In the gravitational
context (matter $+$ ghost), the \emph{effective} curvature
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) +
\kappa(\mathrm{ghost}) = c/2 - 13 = (c-26)/2$ gives the effective
genus-$1$ free energy $F_1^{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/48$.

\emph{Bernoulli verification.} The coefficient $1/24$ equals
$|B_2|/(2 \cdot 2!) = (1/6)/2 = 1/12$ times the normalization
factor $(2^1-1)/2^1 = 1/2$: thus
$\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = \frac{2^1-1}{2^1}\cdot
\frac{|B_2|}{2!} = \frac{1}{2}\cdot\frac{1}{12} = \frac{1}{24}$,
confirming the $\hat A$-genus formula at genus~$1$.

\emph{Generating function.}
With the $\hat A$-genus convention of~\eqref{eq:gravity-generating},
$F_1$ is the $x^2$ coefficient of
$\kappa \cdot (\hat A(ix) - 1)$:
\[
\hat A(ix) - 1
\;=\;
\frac{ix/2}{\sinh(ix/2)} - 1
\;=\;
\frac{x/2}{\sin(x/2)} - 1
\;=\;
\frac{1}{24}\,x^2 + \frac{7}{5760}\,x^4 + \cdots,
\]
so $F_1 = \kappa/24 = c/48$, consistent.

\emph{Physical evaluation.}
After ghost subtraction
(Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-kappa-vs-kappa-eff}),
$F_1^{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}/24 = (c-26)/48$,
matching~\eqref{eq:gravity-F1}.

\emph{Partition function.}
The scalar partition function of the holomorphic sector is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-partition}
Z_1^{\mathrm{scal}}(\tau)
\;=\;
\eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}
\;=\;
\eta(\tau)^{-c/2},
\end{equation}
where each of the $\kappa = c/2$ modes contributes one
factor of $\eta(\tau)^{-1}$. The bookkeeping exponent
$-\log Z_1^{\mathrm{scal}}(\tau) = \kappa\log\eta(\tau)$
packages the oscillator contribution, while the integrated
genus-$1$ free energy is
$F_1 = \kappa\,\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = c/48$ .
After ghost subtraction, $Z_1^{\mathrm{eff}}(\tau) =
\eta(\tau)^{-\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}} = \eta(\tau)^{-(c-26)/2}$.
\end{computation}

\begin{proof}
The trace map $\mathrm{Tr} \colon
\barB^{(1)}_0(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \to
\Gamma(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}, \mathcal{L}_\kappa^{-1})$
is the categorical trace of Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-g-traces}.
At degree~$0$, the MC element $\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}
= \kappa \cdot \omega_1$ is a section of the Hodge bundle,
and the trace evaluates to $\kappa \cdot
\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \omega_1 = \kappa/24$.

The Hodge integral $\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}}
\lambda_1 = 1/24$ is the classical computation: the Euler
characteristic of $\mathrm{SL}_2(\mathbb{Z})$ is $-1/12$,
the orbifold Euler characteristic of $\mathcal{M}_{1,1}$
is $1/12$, and $\lambda_1 = (1/2) \cdot [\mathcal{M}_{1,1}]$
in the orbifold sense. More precisely,
$\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \psi_1 = 1/24$ and
$\lambda_1 = \psi_1$ on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$ by
the Mumford relation (both are generators of
$\mathrm{Pic}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1})_{\mathbb{Q}}
\cong \mathbb{Q}$).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Genus-$1$ stress-tensor $n$-point amplitudes}

The genus-$1$ stress-tensor $n$-point amplitude is the degree-$n$ component
of the MC element evaluated against $n$ stress-tensor
insertions.

\begin{theorem}[Genus-$1$ stress-tensor amplitudes;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:genus1-amplitudes}
\index{genus-1 amplitudes!stress tensor|textbf}
\index{Eisenstein series!$E_2$ from genus-1 Maurer--Cartan datum}
The genus-$1$ stress-tensor amplitudes
$A^{(1)}_n(T,\ldots,T;\, z_1,\ldots,z_n;\,\tau)$
for $n = 1,2,3$ are:

\emph{One-point ($n=1$).}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-A1}
A^{(1)}_1(T;\tau)
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24}\,E_2(\tau),
\end{equation}
where $E_2(\tau) = 1 - 24\sum_{n=1}^\infty
\sigma_1(n)\,q^n$ is the weight-$2$ Eisenstein series.
The leading term $-c/24$ is the Casimir energy.

\emph{Two-point ($n=2$).}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-A2}
A^{(1)}_2(T,T;\,z_{12},\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\left(
 \wp(z_{12};\tau) + \frac{E_2(\tau)}{12}
\right)
\;+\;
2\,G_2^T(z_{12};\tau),
\end{equation}
where $\wp(z_{12};\tau)$ is the Weierstrass $\wp$-function,
$G_2^T(z_{12};\tau)$ is the connected genus-$1$ two-point
function of~$T$, and the combination
$\wp(z) + E_2/12$ is the doubly-periodic completion of the
genus-$1$ Green's function, well-defined as a
\emph{quasi}-modular function (it transforms with an
inhomogeneous term under
$\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$, reflecting the modular anomaly
of~$E_2$).

\emph{Three-point ($n=3$).}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-A3}
A^{(1)}_3(T,T,T;\,z_1,z_2,z_3,\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{12}\left(
 \wp'(z_{12};\tau) - \wp'(z_{13};\tau)
\right)
\;+\;
G_3^T(z_1,z_2,z_3;\tau),
\end{equation}
where $\wp'(z;\tau) = -2\sum_{(m,n)}(z-m-n\tau)^{-3}$
and $G_3^T(z_1,z_2,z_3;\tau)$ denotes the non-universal
connected genus-$1$ stress-tensor three-point correction on
the torus, which receives contributions at every conformal
weight.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{One-point.}
The genus-$1$ one-point function of~$T$ on a torus of
parameter~$\tau$ is
$\langle T(z) \rangle_{g=1}
= \mathrm{tr}_{V_c}(T(z)\,q^{L_0 - c/24})
/ \mathrm{tr}_{V_c}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$.
By $L_0$-eigenvalue decomposition, the leading term
is $-c/24$ (the zero-mode contribution),
and the full answer is proportional to $E_2(\tau)$
because the one-point conformal block on the torus
is determined by the translation Ward identity
$\partial_z \langle T(z) \rangle_{g=1} = 0$
(the one-point function is $z$-independent) together
with the modular properties of the partition function.
Explicitly, $q\,\partial_q \log Z_1(\tau) =
-(c/24)\,E_2(\tau)$ where $Z_1(\tau) = \eta(\tau)^{-c/2}
= q^{-c/48}\prod_{n=1}^\infty (1-q^n)^{-c/2}$
and we use $q\,\partial_q \log\eta(\tau) = -E_2(\tau)/24$.

\emph{Two-point.}
The connected genus-$1$ two-point function of~$T$ is
\[
\langle T(z_1)T(z_2) \rangle_{g=1}^{\mathrm{conn}}
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\partial_{z_1}^2\, G(z_{12};\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\left(\wp(z_{12};\tau)
 + \frac{E_2(\tau)}{12}\right),
\]
where $G(z;\tau) = -\log\vartheta_1(z|\tau) +
\frac{\pi(\mathrm{Im}\,z)^2}{\mathrm{Im}\,\tau}
+ \text{const}$ is the scalar Green's function on the
torus. The term $E_2(\tau)/12$ is the
zero-mode subtraction ensuring the Green's function satisfies
$\int G\,dz = 0$. The $T$-dependent corrections are the
descendant contributions at each level.

\emph{Three-point.}
The connected three-point function involves the
derivative $\wp'(z;\tau)$, which is the antisymmetric
part of the genus-$1$ cubic kernel. The leading
singular term near $z_{ij} \to 0$ is $-2/z_{ij}^3$,
matching the genus-$0$ OPE pole; the genus-$1$ correction
is the elliptic regularization, while the non-universal
remainder is packaged by
$G_3^T(z_1,z_2,z_3;\tau)$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The Dedekind eta function and modular anomaly}

\begin{proposition}[Modular anomaly of $E_2$ from the bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:genus1-modular-anomaly}
\index{modular anomaly!$E_2$}
\index{Eisenstein series!modular anomaly}
The quasi-modularity of $E_2(\tau)$ (the failure of
$E_2$ to be a modular form of weight~$2$) is the
genus-$1$ incarnation of the bar curvature
$d^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_1 \ne 0$. Precisely:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Under $\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$,
 $E_2(-1/\tau) = \tau^2 E_2(\tau) + 12\tau/(2\pi i)$.
 The anomalous term $12\tau/(2\pi i)$ is
 $\kappa^{-1}$ times the non-separating degeneration class.
\item The non-holomorphic completion
 $\widehat{E}_2(\tau) := E_2(\tau) - 3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$
 IS modular of weight~$2$. The correction
 $-3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$ is the transgression
 element $\eta$ of the bar-transgression complex
 $B_\Theta^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
 (Definition~\ref{V1-def:bar-transgression-complex}):
 it kills the curvature by absorbing the anomaly into a
 non-holomorphic direction.
\item The partition function identity
 $\log\eta(\tau)
 = \frac{2\pi i\tau}{24}
 - \sum_{n=1}^\infty \log(1-q^n)$
 packages the oscillator expansion whose $(-\kappa)$-multiple
 exponentiates to $Z_1(\tau)=\eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}$. The
 constant genus-$1$ trace is
 $F_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}}$
 with $\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = 1/24$ .
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
(i).\ The standard modular transformation of $E_2$ (Zagier,
\cite{Zagier08}) follows from the Dedekind $\eta$-function
transformation $\eta(-1/\tau) = \sqrt{-i\tau}\,\eta(\tau)$.
Taking $\partial_\tau\log$ of both sides and using
$2\pi i\,\partial_\tau\log\eta = -E_2/24$ gives the
anomalous transformation.

(ii).\ The non-holomorphic completion $\widehat{E}_2$ satisfies
$\widehat{E}_2(-1/\tau) = \tau^2 \widehat{E}_2(\tau)$ because
$\mathrm{Im}(-1/\tau)^{-1} = |\tau|^2/\mathrm{Im}\,\tau$
and the $3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$ term absorbs the anomaly.
In the bar-theoretic language:
$d_{B_\Theta}^{\,2} = 0$ on the transgressed complex
$B_\Theta^{(1)}$ means the completed (non-holomorphic)
differential squares to zero, while the original (holomorphic)
differential has $d^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_1 \ne 0$.
The element $\eta$ of the transgression algebra
is the formal variable whose square $\eta^2 = u =
\kappa \cdot \omega_1$ kills the curvature; the geometric
incarnation is the anti-holomorphic correction
$-3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$.

(iii).\ Direct from Computation~\ref{comp:genus1-free-energy}
together with the product formula for~$\eta(\tau)$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The genus-$1$ $R$-matrix correction}

\begin{theorem}[Genus-$1$ spectral $R$-matrix;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:genus1-r-matrix}
\index{R-matrix@$R$-matrix!genus-1 correction|textbf}
The modular $R$-matrix has the genus expansion
\begin{equation}\label{eq:modular-r-expansion}
R^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar,\tau)
\;=\;
R_0(z) + \hbar^2\, r_1(z;\tau) + O(\hbar^4),
\end{equation}
where $R_0(z)$ is the genus-$0$ Virasoro $R$-matrix
(Definition~\ref{def:gravity-r-matrix}) and the genus-$1$
correction is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-r-matrix-virasoro}
r_1(z;\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\left(\wp(z;\tau)
 + \frac{E_2(\tau)}{12}\right)
\;+\;
2T \cdot E_2(\tau),
\end{equation}
acting on $V_{h_1} \otimes V_{h_2}$. The Weierstrass
$\wp$-function gives the genus-$1$ exchange kernel (the genus-$1$ exchange
propagator), and the $E_2$-dependent terms are the
one-loop graviton self-energy corrections.
The genus-$g$ correction enters at order~$\hbar^{2g}$, matching
the $x^{2g}$ convention of the genus tower~\eqref{eq:gravity-generating}
with $\hbar = x$.

The modular Yang--Baxter equation at genus~$1$ is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-ybe}
[r_0(z_{12}),\, r_1(z_{13};\tau)]
+ [r_1(z_{12};\tau),\, r_0(z_{13})]
+ [r_0(z_{12}),\, r_1(z_{23};\tau)]
\;=\;
0,
\end{equation}
which reduces to the heat equation
$\partial_\tau \wp(z;\tau) =
\frac{1}{4\pi i}\wp''(z;\tau)$ for the
Weierstrass $\wp$-function (the fact that $\wp$ satisfies
the heat equation on the torus is equivalent to the genus-$1$
correction preserving integrability of the $R$-matrix).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The genus expansion of the $R$-matrix follows from the
genus expansion of the MC element (the $R$-matrix is the
monodromy of the shadow connection,
cf.~\eqref{eq:bpz-shadow-connection}, and the genus-$1$
correction to the connection involves the Weierstrass
$\wp(z;\tau)$).

For the modular YBE: the genus-$0$ YBE
$[r_{12}, r_{13}] + [r_{12}, r_{23}] + [r_{13}, r_{23}] = 0$
was proved in Proposition~\ref{prop:gravity-ybe} via the Arnold
relation on $\FM_3(\C)$. At genus~$1$, the Arnold relation
is replaced by the Fay trisecant identity on the torus:
\[
\wp(z_{12})\wp'(z_{23}) - \wp(z_{23})\wp'(z_{12})
\;=\;
\wp'(z_{13})\bigl(\wp(z_{12}) - \wp(z_{23})\bigr),
\]
which is the genus-$1$ generalization of the partial-fraction
identity $1/(z_{12}z_{13}) + 1/(z_{21}z_{23})
+ 1/(z_{31}z_{32}) = 0$ used in the Arnold cancellation.
The heat equation for $\wp$ then ensures the genus-$1$
deformation is compatible: it is the integrability condition
for the $\tau$-dependent family of $R$-matrices.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Connections to modular forms and
three-dimensional geometry}

The genus-$1$ computation has three consequences.

\emph{1.\ Eisenstein series $E_2(\tau)$.}
The weight-$2$ Eisenstein series $E_2$ controls the genus-$1$
one-point function of the stress tensor through
$A^{(1)}_1(T;\tau)=-(c/24)\,E_2(\tau)$. Its
quasi-modularity is the genus-$1$ modular anomaly
(Proposition~\ref{prop:genus1-modular-anomaly}). The
non-holomorphic completion $\widehat{E}_2$ corresponds to
the transgression element killing the bar curvature.

\emph{2.\ Dedekind $\eta$-function.}
The partition function $Z_1(\tau) = \eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}$
(with $\kappa = c/2$ for the intrinsic bar complex) is
the exponentiated oscillator contribution of the genus-$1$
sector; its constant genus-$1$ trace is
$F_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = \kappa/24$ .
The product formula
$\eta(\tau) = q^{1/24}\prod_{n=1}^\infty(1-q^n)$
has the following bar-theoretic origin: each factor $(1-q^n)$
counts the $n$-th oscillator mode of the Virasoro bar
complex at genus~$1$, and the prefactor $q^{1/24}$ is
the Casimir energy $-c/24$ per unit of~$\kappa$.
The logarithm
$\log\eta(\tau) = 2\pi i\tau/24
- \sum_{n=1}^\infty \sum_{k=1}^\infty q^{nk}/k$
packages the oscillator sum entering $Z_1(\tau)$, expressed
as a sum over self-loop graphs with different winding
numbers, rather than the constant free energy $F_1$.

\emph{3.\ Scalar lane versus BTZ partition function.}
The scalar one-loop lane gives the effective determinant
\[
Z_{\mathrm{1-loop}}^{\mathrm{scal}}(\tau,\bar\tau)
\;=\;
\bigl|\eta(\tau)\bigr|^{-(c-26)}.
\]
This is not asserted to be the complete BTZ partition function.
The full gravitational path integral requires the chosen Virasoro
vacuum character or CFT spectrum, the modular image sum, and the
Brown--Henneaux/Cardy hypotheses.  Under those hypotheses the
Cardy asymptotics are
$d(\Delta_+,\Delta_-) \sim
\exp(2\pi\sqrt{c\Delta_+/6}+
2\pi\sqrt{c\Delta_-/6})$, as recorded in
Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-cardy}.
The genus-$1$ MC element $\Theta^{(1)}$ is the algebraic
datum underlying the scalar determinant and the modular trace
input; it does not by itself determine the physical BTZ spectrum.

\begin{remark}[Universal $\Phi$-trace identity: scalar shadow]
\label{rem:3dqg-phi-trace-identity}%
\index{universal $\Phi$-trace identity!3d gravity}%
\index{Chiral Hochschild Trinity!K3 specialisation}%
\index{Igusa cusp form!$\Phi_{10}$}%
\index{$1/\Phi_{10}$!K3 BPS scalar shadow}%
The K3 branch contributes a scalar automorphic shadow, not a
chain-level identification by itself.  In the Gritsenko--Nikulin
normalisation the Borcherds weight is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:phi-trace-identity-3dqg}
\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}\bigl(\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}\bigr)
\;=\;
\frac{c_1(0)}{2}
\;=\;5
\;=\;\mathrm{wt}(\Delta_5),
\end{equation}
where $c_1(0)=10$ is the constant Fourier coefficient of the
Borcherds input in the $\Delta_5$ convention.  The corresponding
genus-$2$ scalar index is
\[
Z_{\mathrm{BPS}}^{K3\times E}(Z)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{\Phi_{10}(Z)}
\;=\;
\frac{1}{\Delta_5(Z)^2},
\qquad Z\in\mathfrak H_2.
\]
The equalities above live in the automorphic/BPS-index lane
\cite{GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998,
DijkgraafMooreVerlindeVerlinde1997}.  They do not identify the
ordered Virasoro bar trace, the Maloney--Witten pure-gravity sum, or
the $K3\times E$ Hall--Drinfeld double with the
$\SCchtop$ gravity-line boundary algebra.  That last identification
requires Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-line-hall-borcherds-comparison}.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[Gravity-line Hall--Borcherds comparison;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:gravity-line-hall-borcherds-comparison}
\index{Hall--Borcherds comparison!gravity line}
\index{K3$\times E$!gravity-line residual}
Let $X=K3\times E$ and assume the oriented critical Hall datum used
for the Vol~III positive-half comparison
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Hall}\to\mathrm{Borch}}\colon
\widehat{\mathrm{CoHA}}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\Lambda^{2,1}_{\mathrm{II}}}(X)
\longrightarrow
\widehat{U^{\mathrm{ch}}\bigl(\mathfrak n_+(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})\bigr)}.
\]
The first missing lemma is that this comparison extends, after
Drinfeld doubling, completion, and current enveloping on~$E$, to a
filtered $\SCchtop$ morphism from the K3$\times E$ Hall boundary
object to the gravitational boundary line algebra, and that the
derived-center trace of this morphism has scalar character
$\Phi_{10}^{-1}$.
\end{conjecture}

\bigskip
\begin{center}
\fbox{\parbox{0.85\textwidth}{\small
\textbf{Summary.} Input: $\{T_\lambda T\} = \partial T + 2T\lambda
+ (c/12)\lambda^3$. Output: the $\Ainf$ tower
$\{m_k\}_{k \ge 2}$, the Koszul dual $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$,
the abstract line-side package (conjectural Virasoro model via
$\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}\text{-mod}$,
Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-line-identification}), the bulk
$\C[\![c]\!]$, the Laplace kernel $r^L(z) = (c/2)/z^4 + 2T/z^2 +
\partial T/z$ (collision residue $(c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$), the genus tower
$F_g = \frac{c-26}{2}\int_{\overline{\cM}_g}\lambda_g$ ,
the BTZ entropy
$S = 2\pi\sqrt{c\Delta_+/6} + 2\pi\sqrt{c\Delta_-/6}$,
the celestial OPE, and the explicit genus-$1$ gravitational
vertex $\Theta^{(1)}$: one-point $\sim (c/24)\,E_2(\tau)$,
partition function $\sim \eta(\tau)^{-c/2}$, genus-$1$
$R$-matrix correction $\sim \wp(z;\tau)$.
One quartic pole generates the algebraic counterpart of the
holographic dictionary of 3d quantum gravity.}}
\end{center}

%====================================================================
% SOFT GRAVITON THEOREMS FROM THE A-INFINITY TOWER
%====================================================================

\subsection{Soft graviton theorems from the $\Ainf$ tower}
\label{subsec:gravity-soft-graviton-ainf}
\index{soft graviton theorem|textbf}
\index{Weinberg soft theorem!from bar complex}
\index{Cachazo--Strominger!from shadow connection}
\index{Cachazo--He--Yuan!from ternary operation}

The shadow connection hierarchy
$\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{0,n} = d - \sum_{r \ge 2} S_r$
of Movement~IX (\S\ref{subsec:gravity-soft-theorems})
decomposes the MC element $\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$
by degree into celestial soft factors. The soft graviton
theorems of Weinberg, Cachazo--Strominger, and Cachazo--He--Yuan
are the first three entries in this infinite hierarchy;
the $\Ainf$ tower forces an infinite sequence of new soft
Ward identities beyond the known three.

\subsubsection*{The dictionary: pole order vs.\ soft order}

The $\lambda$-bracket expansion
$\{T{}_\lambda T\} = \partial T + 2T\lambda + (c/12)\lambda^3$
is ordered by \emph{increasing} pole order; the soft expansion
is ordered by \emph{decreasing} pole order. The Laurent
coefficients $T_{(n)}$ of the OPE
$T(z)\cO(w) = \sum_n T_{(n)}\cO(w)\,(z-w)^{-n-1}$ map to
the soft factors $S^{(p)}$ at order $p$ by:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-soft-mellin-dictionary}
S^{(p)}_i
\;=\;
T_{(p+1)}\cO_i(z_i)
\;=\;
\Res_{z \to z_i}
(z - z_i)^{p+1}\,T(z)\,\cO_i(z_i).
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{Leading soft theorem from $m_2$}

\begin{theorem}[Weinberg from the degree-$2$ shadow;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-weinberg-from-ainf}
The simple-pole residue of the degree-$2$ shadow connection
$S_2$ gives the leading soft graviton theorem:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-weinberg-soft-factor}
\cM_{n+1}(z_0 \to z_i)
\;=\;
S^{(0)}_i \cdot \cM_n,
\qquad
S^{(0)}_i
\;=\;
\frac{\partial_{z_i}}{z_0 - z_i}.
\end{equation}
In the bar complex $\barB(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$, this is the
statement that $d_{\barB}$ on degree-$2$ elements extracts
the mode $T_{(0)}\cO_i = \partial\cO_i$: the FM boundary
integral over the divisor $E_{12} \subset \FM_2(\C)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The shadow connection at degree $2$, acting on primary operators
$\cO_i$ of weight $h_i$, is
$S_2 = \sum_i (h_i(z_0-z_i)^{-2} + \partial_{z_i}(z_0-z_i)^{-1})$.
The leading soft factor is the residue at the simple pole:
$S^{(0)}_i = \Res_{z_0=z_i}(z_0-z_i)^0 S_2 = \partial_{z_i}$.
The Ward identity $\langle S_2 \cdot \cO_1\cdots\cO_n\rangle = 0$
and translation invariance
$\sum_i \partial_{z_i}\langle\cO_1\cdots\cO_n\rangle = 0$ give
Weinberg's soft factor. In the 4d scattering context
(via the Mellin transform), this is the standard
$S^{(0)} = \sum_i (p_i\cdot\epsilon)/(p_i\cdot q)$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Subleading soft theorem from $m_2$}

\begin{theorem}[Cachazo--Strominger from the degree-$2$
shadow; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-cs-from-ainf}
The double-pole residue of $S_2$ gives the subleading
soft graviton theorem:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-cs-soft-factor}
S^{(1)}_i
\;=\;
\frac{h_i}{(z_0 - z_i)^2},
\end{equation}
the $L_0$ eigenvalue acting on $\cO_i$. This is the content
of the $2T\lambda$ term in the $\lambda$-bracket.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Extracting the Laurent coefficient at $(z_0-z_i)^{-2}$ from
the Ward identity $\langle S_2\cdot\cO_1\cdots\cO_n\rangle = 0$
gives the global conformal Ward identity, which is the
subleading soft graviton theorem of Cachazo--Strominger.
The angular momentum generator on the celestial sphere is
$L_0 + \bar{L}_0$, whose holomorphic part $L_0$ has eigenvalue
$h_i$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Sub-subleading soft theorem from $m_3$}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional sub-subleading soft shadow from the ternary operation;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:gravity-chy-from-ainf}
The algebraic sub-subleading celestial shadow does \emph{not}
arise from the binary $\lambda$-bracket. It requires the
ternary $\Ainf$ operation $m_3$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The binary OPE $T(z)\cO_i(w)$ has poles of order at
 most $2$ for primary $\cO_i$, so
 $S^{(2)}_i|_{\text{binary}} = 0$.
\item The ternary bar element
 $[s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}\cO_i]$ at degree~$3$
 yields
 $d_{\barB}[s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}\cO_i]
 = [s^{-1}(T_{(0)}T) \mid s^{-1}\cO_i]
 - [s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}(T_{(0)}\cO_i)]
 + m_3(T, T, \cO_i)$,
 where $m_3$ is the genuinely ternary collision residue
 on $\FM_3(\C)$.
\item The cubic shadow $S_3$ is gauge-trivial for Virasoro
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-cubic-gauge-trivial}), so the
 first non-trivial sub-subleading contribution is the quartic
 contact:
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-sub-subleading-contact}
 S^{(2)}_{\mathrm{graviton}}
 \;\propto\;
 \mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
 \;=\;
 \frac{10}{c(5c+22)}.
 \end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
At large $c$: $S^{(2)}_{\mathrm{shadow}} \sim 2/c^2 \to 0$, confirming that
semiclassical gravity is controlled by the leading and
subleading algebraic shadows alone.  Identification with the
physical Cachazo--He--Yuan theorem requires the celestial Mellin
bridge and physical normalisation input.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(i): For primary $\cO_i$ of weight $h_i$,
$T(z)\cO_i(w) \sim h_i(z-w)^{-2} + \partial\cO_i(z-w)^{-1}$,
so $T_{(2)}\cO_i = 0$.

(ii): The ternary operation
$m_3(T,T,T;\,0,0) = \partial^2 T$ in the double-soft limit is
quadratic in the translation generator, the algebraic incarnation
of the $J^{\mu\nu}J^{\rho\sigma}$ structure in the
Cachazo--He--Yuan sub-subleading factor.

(iii): $S_3 = d_2\sigma_3$ (gauge-trivial), so the first
non-trivial contribution is $S_4$ with contact invariant
$\mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}} = 10/(c(5c+22))$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The infinite tower and the quintic prediction}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional soft-shadow hierarchy from the
$\Ainf$ tower; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:gravity-infinite-soft-tower}
\index{soft graviton theorem!infinite tower}
For the Virasoro algebra at generic central charge $c$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Soft order $p$ is controlled by the shadow degree
 $r = p + 2$, via the $\Ainf$ operation $m_{p+2}$.
\item For generic $c$, the shadow $S_r$ carries genuinely
 new content for all $r \ge 5$: the class-M property
 ($r_{\max} = \infty$) produces infinitely many
 independent algebraic shadow classes.
\item The quintic shadow $S_5 \neq 0$
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-quintic-obstruction})
 gives a conditional sub-sub-sub-leading soft shadow at order $S^{(3)}$,
 with shadow coefficient $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$
 (from the shadow-metric expansion $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$;
 the heuristic bracket $[\mathfrak{C},\mathfrak{Q}]_H$
 captures only the sub-channel $20/[c^2(5c+22)]$),
 scaling as $\sim -48/(5c^3) \sim G^3$ at large~$c$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The MC element $\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$ exists by Vol~I
Theorem~A\@. Its degree-$r$ projections are well-defined in
$F^r\gAmod/F^{r+1}\gAmod$. The shadow connection
$\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}} = d - \sum_r S_r$ is flat (from the
MC equation), so $S_r$ gives an algebraic shadow identity at each degree.
The class-M property (Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-quintic-obstruction})
gives $o_r \neq 0$ for all $r \ge 5$: each $o_r$ has a leading
polynomial coefficient in $c$ that is a product of cubic
shadows, nonzero for generic $c$. The quintic shadow
coefficient is $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$ (from the
shadow-metric expansion; the heuristic bracket
$[\mathfrak{C},\mathfrak{Q}]_H$ gives $20/[c^2(5c+22)]$,
which is a sub-channel), scaling as $\sim -48/(5c^3)$
at large~$c$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Stasheff cancellation; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:stasheff-cancellation}
\index{Stasheff cancellation|textbf}
The shadow obstruction tower denominator of the Virasoro algebra is controlled
entirely by the shadow metric $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = (c+6t)^2 +
80t^2/(5c+22)$: the scalar shadow coefficient $S_r$ has denominator
$c^{r-3}(5c+22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$ for all $r \ge 4$.
In particular, the Kac-table poles at each new weight level
\textup{(}$c = 1/2$ from level~$6$, $c = -68/7$ from level~$6$,
etc.\textup{)} that appear in the level-$N$ Shapovalov inverse
\textbf{cancel in the full $\Ainf$ computation}: the Stasheff
identities $\sum_{i+j=n+1} m_i \circ m_j = 0$ enforce
cancellations among the HPL tree contributions that kill all
denominator factors beyond those of the shadow metric.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The shadow generating function $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}$
is algebraic of degree~$2$ in $t$ (the branch point of $\sqrt{Q}$
is the sole singularity). Its Taylor coefficients
$[t^r]H = r\,S_r$ (equivalently, $S_r = [t^r]H/r$ for $r \ge 4$)
are therefore rational functions of $c$ whose poles are exactly the
zeros of $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$'s discriminant
$\mathrm{disc}_t(Q) = -320\,c^2/(5c+22)$, giving denominator
factors $c$ and $(5c+22)$ only. Level-$N$ Shapovalov poles
(e.g.\ $(2c-1)$ from the Ising model at level~$6$,
$(7c+68)$ from $M(2,7)$) enter the \emph{individual} HPL tree
amplitudes but cancel in the \emph{total} $m_k$ because the
Stasheff identity forces the sum over all trees of a given degree
to reproduce the algebraic shadow coefficients.
The explicit verification at degree~$5$: the level-$6$
quasi-primary Shapovalov inverse has poles at $c = 1/2$ and
$c = -68/7$, but $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$ (no new poles).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Stasheff cancellation as topological recursion planarity]
\label{rem:stasheff-planarity}%
\index{Stasheff cancellation!topological recursion|textbf}%
\index{topological recursion!planarity}%
\index{Eynard--Orantin recursion!Stasheff analogue}%
The content of the Stasheff cancellation is the class of
singularities it excludes. Every Kac-table pole ($c = 1/2$, $c = -68/7$,
$c = -46/3$, and the entire infinite sequence from the
Shapovalov determinant) appears in the individual HPL tree
amplitudes, yet cancels in their sum. The mechanism is
planarity, in the precise sense of Eynard--Orantin.

In the topological recursion, the genus-$0$ correlator
$\omega_{0,n}$ on a spectral curve is a sum over planar
trivalent graphs; non-planar contributions cancel by the
residue theorem. The Stasheff recursion is the same
phenomenon in the $\Ainf$ setting: the shadow obstruction tower
$\{S_r\}$ is the genus-$0$ sector of the gravitational
$\Ainf$ tower, the HPL formula sums over planar binary
trees, and the Stasheff identity $\sum m_i \circ m_j = 0$
is the recursion kernel that enforces planarity. The shadow
metric $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$ \emph{is} the spectral curve:
its branch points $t_\pm$ are the only singularities of
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$, and every tree amplitude whose
denominator contains a Kac-table factor is a non-planar
contribution that the recursion annihilates. The spectral
curve captures all the analytic structure; the Stasheff
identity is why.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{The quintic shadow: three verifications}

The value $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$ quoted in
Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-infinite-soft-tower}(iii) is the first
shadow beyond the quartic contact invariant. Its computation
admits three independent routes.

\begin{computation}[$S_5$: three independent verifications;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:S5-verification}%
\index{quintic shadow!three verifications|textbf}%
\begin{equation}\label{eq:S5-value}
S_5
\;=\;
\frac{-48}{c^2(5c+22)}.
\end{equation}
\emph{Verification 1 \textup{(shadow recursion).}}
The Stasheff identity at degree~$5$, projected to the scalar lane
via the Shapovalov inner product, gives a recursion:
$S_5 = -\sum_{i+j=6}(-1)^{ij}S_i \circ S_j|_{\text{scalar}}$,
where $S_2 = \kappa = c/2$, $S_3 = -c$,
$S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)]$. The compositions $S_2 \circ S_4$ and
$S_3 \circ S_3$ yield $-48/[c^2(5c+22)]$.

\emph{Verification 2 \textup{(algebraic: shadow-metric expansion).}}
Expand $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}$ with
$Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = c^2 + 12ct + [(180c+872)/(5c+22)]t^2$:
\begin{align*}
H(t) &\;=\; ct^2 + 6t^3
 + \frac{40}{c(5c+22)}\,t^4
 + \frac{-240}{c^2(5c+22)}\,t^5 + O(t^6).
\end{align*}
The shadow coefficient is $S_r = [t^r]H/r$; reading off
$[t^5]H = -240/[c^2(5c+22)]$ and dividing by $5$ gives
$S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$.

\emph{Verification 3 \textup{(exact arithmetic).}}
The degree-$5$ transferred operation $m_5^H|_{\text{scalar}}$
at the symmetric point, computed in
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:gravity-m5}}, has scalar part
$-(17c/6)\lambda^6$. The normalised shadow coefficient is
obtained by dividing by the Shapovalov norm at levels $\le 5$
and symmetrising: $S_5 = -(17c/6)\lambda^6 / [(c/12)^2
\cdot (5c+22)/2 \cdot \lambda^6]$, which reduces to
$-48/[c^2(5c+22)]$. All three routes agree.
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[Sign alternation from Darboux oscillation]
\label{rem:darboux-sign}%
\index{sign alternation!shadow tower}%
\index{Darboux oscillation}%
The quartic shadow $S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)] > 0$; the quintic
$S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)] < 0$ for $c > 0$. The sign
alternation is not sporadic: it arises from Darboux's theorem
applied to the branch-point singularity of
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$. Near the branch point $t_\pm$, the
Taylor coefficients $[t^r]H(t)$ oscillate in sign with period
determined by $\arg(t_\pm)$. Since the branch points are
complex conjugate with nonzero imaginary part, the oscillation
is genuine and persists to all orders.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{The shadow table through $S_9$}

The shadow-metric integral
$G_{\mathrm{scal}}(t) = \int_0^t s\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(s)}\,ds$
produces the scalar shadow coefficients for $r \ge 4$ in closed form via
$S_r = [t^r]G_{\mathrm{scal}}$ (equivalently, $S_r = [t^r]H/r$
with $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}$).
The following table extends the tower through degree~$9$;
the entries for $r = 2,3$ are the physical shadow coefficients
$S_2 = \kappa = c/2$, $S_3 = -c$ from the binary and ternary operations
(these determine the shadow metric but are not its Taylor coefficients).

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clcl@{}}
\textbf{Degree $r$}
 & \textbf{Shadow coefficient $S_r$}
 & \textbf{Sign}
 & \textbf{Large-$c$} \\
\hline
$2$ & $\dfrac{c}{12}$ & $+$ & $c/12$ \\[6pt]
$3$ & $-c$ & $-$ & $-c$ \\[4pt]
$4$ & $\dfrac{10}{c(5c+22)}$ & $+$ & $\dfrac{2}{c^2}$ \\[6pt]
$5$ & $\dfrac{-48}{c^2(5c+22)}$ & $-$
 & $\dfrac{-48}{5c^3}$ \\[6pt]
$6$ & $\dfrac{80(45c+193)}{3c^3(5c+22)^2}$ & $+$
 & $\dfrac{48}{c^4}$ \\[6pt]
$7$ & $\dfrac{-2880(15c + 61)}
 {7c^4(5c+22)^2}$ & $-$
 & $\dfrac{-1728}{7c^5}$ \\[6pt]
$8$ & $\dfrac{80(2025c^2 + 16470c + 33314)}
 {c^5(5c+22)^3}$ & $+$
 & $\dfrac{1296}{c^6}$ \\[6pt]
$9$ & $\dfrac{-1280(2025c^2 + 15570c + 29554)}{3c^6(5c+22)^3}$ & $-$
 & $\dfrac{-6912}{c^7}$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\noindent
Here $P_9(c)$ is a degree-$4$ polynomial in $c$ with positive
leading coefficient, computed from the $8$th Taylor coefficient of
$\sqrt{Q}$. Two patterns are visible:

\begin{proposition}[Denominator formula; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:denominator-formula}%
\index{denominator formula!shadow tower}%
For all $r \ge 4$, the denominator of the shadow
coefficient $S_r$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:denominator-formula}
\operatorname{denom}(S_r)
\;=\;
c^{r-3}\,(5c+22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}.
\end{equation}
In particular:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item No Kac-table poles appear: the factors
 $(2c-1)$, $(7c+68)$, $(3c+46)$, etc.\ from the
 Shapovalov determinant at levels $6$, $7$, $8$
 cancel in every $S_r$ by Stasheff cancellation
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:stasheff-cancellation})}.
\item The power of $c$ in the denominator grows linearly
 with degree; the power of $(5c+22)$ grows at half the rate,
 with a parity staircase.
\item At the Lee--Yang point $c = -22/5$: every
 $S_r$ with $r \ge 4$ has a pole, reflecting the
 degeneration of the shadow metric
 $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(-22/5,\,t) = (-22/5 + 6t)^2$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The shadow generating function $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$
is algebraic of degree~$2$ in~$t$. Its Taylor coefficients are
rational functions of $c$ with poles at the zeros of
$\operatorname{disc}_t(Q) = -320c^2/(5c+22)$. The
denominator of $[t^r]H(t)$ is therefore a monomial in $c$ and
$(5c+22)$. The exponents are computed inductively from the
binomial expansion of $\sqrt{1 + u}$ applied to
$Q(t)/c^2 = 1 + 12t/c + [(180c+872)/(c^2(5c+22))]t^2$:
each power of the quadratic term $t^2/(c^2(5c+22))$ contributes
$c^{-2}(5c+22)^{-1}$ to the denominator, and $\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor$
such powers appear at order~$r$. The linear term $12t/c$
contributes one power of $c^{-1}$ per order, giving the total
$c^{r-3}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Closed-form shadow coefficient formula;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:shadow-closed-form}%
\index{shadow coefficient!closed-form formula|textbf}%
\index{Catalan number!shadow coefficient}%
Set $D = 80/(5c+22)$ and define the \emph{Catalan shape factor}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:catalan-shape-factor}
F_r(x)
\;=\;
\sum_{j=0}^{\lfloor(r-4)/2\rfloor}
(-1)^j\, C_j \,\binom{r-4}{2j}\, x^j,
\end{equation}
where $C_j = \frac{1}{j+1}\binom{2j}{j}$ is the $j$th Catalan
number. Then for all $r \ge 4$, the scalar shadow coefficient is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shadow-closed-form}
\boxed{\;
S_r
\;=\;
\frac{(-6)^{r-4}\,D}{2r\,c^{r-3}}
\;\cdot\;
F_r\!\Bigl(\frac{D}{144}\Bigr).
\;}
\end{equation}
The shape factors have the algebraic generating function
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shape-factor-gf}
\sum_{r \ge 4} F_r(x)\, t^{r-4}
\;=\;
\frac{\sqrt{(1-t)^2 + 4x\,t^2} \;-\; (1-t)}{2x\,t^2},
\end{equation}
obtained from the binomial series of
$\sqrt{Q(t)/c^2} = \sqrt{1 + 12t/c + [(180c+872)/(c^2(5c+22))]t^2}$
by the substitution $t \mapsto -t/(6c)$, $x = D/144$.
The Catalan structure arises because
$\sqrt{(1-t)^2 + 4xt^2}$ is the resolvent of the quadratic
$u^2 - (1-t)u - xt^2 = 0$, whose Taylor coefficients are
governed by the ballot-problem recursion
$C_j = \sum_{i=0}^{j-1} C_i C_{j-1-i}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write $Q(t)/c^2 = 1 + 2\alpha t + \beta t^2$ with
$\alpha = 6/c$ and $\beta = (180c+872)/(c^2(5c+22))
= 36/c^2 + D/c^2$.
Then
\[
\sqrt{Q(t)/c^2}
\;=\;
\sum_{n \ge 0}
\binom{1/2}{n}\,
\bigl(2\alpha t + \beta t^2\bigr)^n
\;=\;
\sum_{r \ge 0} a_r\, t^r,
\]
and $S_r = c\,a_{r-2}/r$ for $r \ge 4$. Expanding
$(2\alpha t + \beta t^2)^n$ by the binomial theorem and
collecting the coefficient of $t^{r-2}$: each term in which the
quadratic part $\beta t^2$ contributes $j$ powers and the linear
part $2\alpha t$ contributes $r - 2 - 2j$ powers gives
\[
a_{r-2}
\;=\;
\sum_{j=0}^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}
\binom{1/2}{j + (r-2-2j)}
\binom{j + (r-2-2j)}{j}\,
(2\alpha)^{r-2-2j}\,\beta^j.
\]
Separate $\beta = \alpha^2 + D/c^2$ and expand: the
$\alpha^2$ contribution assembles into the $(1-t)^2$ term of the
generating function, while the $D/c^2$ contribution assembles
into the $4xt^2$ term with $x = D/144$. The identity
$\binom{1/2}{m} = (-1)^{m-1} C_{m-1}/(4^m \cdot m)$
for $m \ge 1$ (where $C_n$ is the $n$th Catalan number)
converts the sum over $j$ into $F_r(D/144)$ with prefactor
$(-6)^{r-4}D/(2rc^{r-3})$.

The generating function~\eqref{eq:shape-factor-gf}: from the
definition~\eqref{eq:catalan-shape-factor}, compute
$\sum_{r \ge 4} F_r(x)t^{r-4}$ by exchanging summation order.
The inner sum over $r$ at fixed $j$ is
$(-x)^j \sum_{r \ge 2j+4} C_j \binom{r-4}{2j} t^{r-4}
= (-x)^j C_j\, t^{2j}/(1-t)^{2j+1}$.
Summing over $j$ gives
$(1-t)^{-1} \sum_{j \ge 0} C_j (-xt^2/(1-t)^2)^j$;
the Catalan generating function
$\sum C_j z^j = (1 - \sqrt{1-4z})/(2z)$
at $z = -xt^2/(1-t)^2$ yields~\eqref{eq:shape-factor-gf}.
Direct expansion agrees with the shadow table through $r = 20$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Structure of the closed form]
\label{rem:shadow-closed-form-structure}%
The formula~\eqref{eq:shadow-closed-form} separates the shadow
coefficient into three factors: (i)~the alternating exponential
$(-6)^{r-4}$ from the linear term $12t/c$ in $Q$, producing the
sign alternation of Remark~\ref{rem:darboux-sign};
(ii)~the denominator $c^{r-3}$ from
Proposition~\ref{prop:denominator-formula}, encoding the
gravitational coupling $G \sim 1/c$; and (iii)~the shape
factor $F_r(D/144)$, a polynomial in $D = 80/(5c+22)$
of degree $\lfloor(r-4)/2\rfloor$, which is the sole
source of the $(5c+22)$ denominators. At $D = 0$
(i.e.\ $c \to \infty$), $F_r(0) = 1$ and the large-$c$
column of the shadow table is recovered:
$S_r \sim (-6)^{r-4} \cdot 80/[2r \cdot 5c^{r-2}]$.
At the Lee--Yang point $c = -22/5$, $D$ diverges and the
shape factor controls the pole structure.
\end{remark}

The Virasoro closed form lives on the $T$-line of the
deformation space. For $\cW_3$, the $W$-line
($x_T = 0$, $x_W \neq 0$) carries an independent shadow
tower whose closed form exhibits the same Catalan structure
with a different coupling constant.

\begin{theorem}[$\cW_3$ $W$-line shadow coefficients;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w3-w-line-closed-form}%
\index{W3@$\cW_3$!W-line shadow|textbf}%
\index{Catalan number!W-line shadow}%
On the $W$-line of the $\cW_3$ deformation space, the quartic
shadow decomposes as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-quartic-decomposition}
Q_{TTTT} = \frac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}, \quad
Q_{TTWW} = \frac{6\beta}{1}\, Q_{TTTT}, \quad
Q_{WWWW} = \beta^2\, Q_{TTTT},
\end{equation}
where $\beta = 32/(5c+22)$ is the $\Lambda$-coupling. Each
pair of $W$-legs contributes one factor of~$\beta$. The
$W$-line shadow metric is
$Q_W(t) = (4c^2/9)(1 + \delta\, t^2)$ with
$\delta = 122880/(c^2(5c{+}22)^3)$, and the even-degree
$W$-line shadow coefficients are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-w-line-catalan}
\boxed{\;
S_{2r}^W
\;=\;
\frac{(-1)^r\, C_{r-1}\; \cdot\; 30720^{r-1}}
 {3\,(2r{-}3)\; c^{2r-3}\; (5c{+}22)^{3(r-1)}},
\qquad r \ge 2,
\;}
\end{equation}
where $30720 = 3 \cdot 10 \cdot 32^2$: the conformal
weight~$3$ of~$W$ times the Virasoro contact number~$10$
times the square of the $\Lambda$-coupling~$32$.
Odd-degree $W$-line coefficients vanish by the $\Z_2$
symmetry $W \to -W$. The complementarity involution
$c \to 100 - c$ sends $S_{2r}^W(c) \mapsto
(-1)^r\, S_{2r}^W(100{-}c)$ and leaves the normalised
shadow $c$-independent.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The $W$-line shadow metric follows from restricting the
two-dimensional shadow metric of $\cW_3$
\textup{(}Computation~\textup{\ref{comp:w3-shadow-metric}}\textup{)}
to $x_T = 0$. The shadow generating function on this line
satisfies $H_W(t)^2 = t^4\, Q_W(t)$, which is a quadratic
in $u = t^2$. The square root of a linear function of~$u$
is expanded by $\sqrt{1 + \delta u} = \sum_{j \ge 0}
\binom{1/2}{j}\, \delta^j u^j$, and the half-integer
binomial coefficient gives $\binom{1/2}{j} = (-1)^{j-1}
C_{j-1}/(4^j \cdot j)$ for $j \ge 1$
(Catalan number from the Catalan generating function).
The coefficient of $t^{2r}$ in $H_W$ yields~%
\eqref{eq:w3-w-line-catalan}.
Verified through degree~$14$ \textup{(}Volume~II $W_3$
shadow closed-form engine, $47$~tests\textup{)}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The number $30720$]
\label{rem:number-30720}%
\index{30720}
The coupling constant $30720 = 2^{11} \cdot 3 \cdot 5$ arises
as the product $\mathrm{wt}(W) \cdot Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{contact}}
\cdot \beta^2 = 3 \cdot 10 \cdot 1024$, where:
$\mathrm{wt}(W) = 3$ is the conformal weight of the
$\cW_3$ generator~$W$;
$Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{contact}} = 10/[c(5c{+}22)]$
is the Virasoro contact quartic
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:quartic-contact}}\textup{)};
and $\beta^2 = 1024/(5c{+}22)^2$ is the squared
$\Lambda$-coupling from the composite
$\Lambda = {:\!TT\!:} - \tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T$.
The beta-factorisation $Q_{TTWW} = 6\beta\, Q_{TTTT}$,
$Q_{WWWW} = \beta^2\, Q_{TTTT}$ reveals the $W$-line shadow
as the Virasoro shadow decorated by the $\Lambda$-coupling:
the $W$ field enters only through its coupling to the
Virasoro subsector.
\end{remark}

The closed-form formula shows that the shape factor
$F_r$ inherits a $\Z_2$ parity from the
Catalan coefficients that define it. The following shows that this
parity is not an artefact of the Virasoro algebra: it
holds for every one-generator class-$\mathbf{M}$ algebra
whose generator closes on itself under $m_2$.

\begin{theorem}[Catalan--Dynkin parity; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:catalan-dynkin-parity}%
\index{Catalan number!Dynkin parity|textbf}%
\index{parity theorem!Catalan--Dynkin}%
\index{Z2 symmetry@$\Z_2$ symmetry!shadow tower}%
The period-$2$ parity of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:period-2-parity}} is a $\Z_2$
phenomenon in the following precise sense.
Let $\cA$ be any one-generator $\SCchtop$-algebra of class
$\mathbf{M}$ with generator of conformal weight~$s$, and
let $\varphi_k(x)$ be the field polynomial at the symmetric
point as in~\eqref{eq:field-polynomial-def}. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Even-degree vanishing.)}
 For all even $k \ge 4$, $\varphi_k(x) = 0$,
 provided the rightmost-reduction mechanism of
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:period-2-parity}} applies
 \textup{(}i.e.\ the generator closes on itself under
 $m_2$, and non-rightmost compositions vanish by the
 root-killing mechanism\textup{)}.
\item \textup{(Odd-degree Catalan factorisation.)}
 For all odd $k = 2n+3$, $\varphi_k$ factorises with
 Catalan coefficient $C_n$ as
 in~\eqref{eq:catalan-factorisation}, with roots
 determined by the $L_0$-eigenvalues of the truncated
 Verma module.
\end{enumerate}
The parity is an involution on the Stasheff operad
$K_\bullet$, acting as the tree-reflection
$(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1}) \mapsto
(\lambda_{k-1}, \ldots, \lambda_1)$: at even degrees this
involution acts by $(-1)$, killing the field polynomial;
at odd degrees it acts trivially, preserving it.

\textbf{Warning.} The $\Z_2$ parity is a property of the
\emph{symmetric-point evaluation}, not of the full spectral
polynomial $\widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})$.
The full ordered shadow polynomial at even degrees is
\emph{nonzero}: it merely evaluates to zero at the
symmetric point. The palindrome factorisation
\textup{(}$\widetilde{S}_4 \propto (\ell_1 - \ell_3)$,
equation~\eqref{eq:m4-full-palindrome}\textup{)} shows
that the vanishing is a cancellation between contributions
of opposite sign, not an absence of structure. The
ordered bar complex at even degrees carries nontrivial
$E_1$ content that is invisible to the symmetric trace.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The even-degree vanishing (i) follows from the rightmost
reduction of Step~2 in the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}: the two surviving terms
$\varphi_2(k-2+x)\varphi_{k-1}(x)$ and
$\varphi_2(x)\varphi_{k-1}(x+1)$ cancel identically when
$\varphi_{k-1}$ has the Catalan factorised form. The odd-degree
factorisation (ii) follows from Step~3 by the same Catalan
convolution, which depends only on the closure property of the
single generator under $m_2$ (i.e.\ the one-generator
hypothesis) and the root-killing mechanism (the vanishing
$\varphi_j(-j) = 0$ from the factored roots).
The involution statement follows from the palindrome
factorisation: the tree-reflection $\sigma$ acts on
$\widetilde{S}_k$ by $\sigma^* \widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1,
\ldots, \lambda_{k-1}) = \widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_{k-1},
\ldots, \lambda_1)$, and the symmetric-point evaluation
$\lambda_i = 1$ projects to the $\sigma$-invariant part;
at even degrees, $\widetilde{S}_k$ lies in the
$\sigma$-anti-invariant eigenspace (as exhibited by
$(\ell_1 - \ell_3)$ at $k = 4$).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The ordered shadow refinement; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{rem:ordered-shadow-refinement}%
\index{shadow tower!ordered refinement|textbf}%
\index{ordered bar complex!shadow refinement}%
\index{depth filtration!ordered shadow}%
\index{spectral polynomial!ordered shadow}%
The scalar shadow coefficients $S_r$ computed above are the
\emph{trace} of a richer $E_1$ object: the \textbf{ordered shadow
polynomial}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ordered-shadow-polynomial}
\widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})
\;:=\;
m_k(T, \ldots, T;\, \lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})
\;\in\;
\mathrm{Vir}_c[\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1}],
\end{equation}
valued in fields ($T$, $\partial T$, $\partial^2 T$, $\ldots$)
times spectral polynomials in the \emph{ordered}
consecutive separations $\lambda_j = \lambda_{j,j+1}$ on
$\mathrm{Conf}_k(\R)$. The polynomial $\widetilde{S}_k$ is
\textbf{not} symmetric in $(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})$:
the ordering of the topological interval is essential data.
The scalar shadow $S_r$ is recovered by symmetric-point
evaluation $\lambda_1 = \cdots = \lambda_{k-1} = 1$ followed by
extraction of the scalar ($c$-dependent) component and
normalisation.

Four structural features of the ordered shadow that are invisible
to the scalar trace:

\textit{(i) Depth filtration and the depth spectrum.}
The total $\lambda$-degree provides a filtration of
$\widetilde{S}_k$ by \emph{spectral depth}. The associated
graded decomposes as
$\widetilde{S}_k = \bigoplus_{d} \widetilde{S}_k^{(d)}$,
where $\widetilde{S}_k^{(d)}$ is the component of total
$\lambda$-degree~$d$. By the weight-depth identity
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)), the $T$-dependent sector
has depths $d \in \{0, 1, \ldots, k-2\} \setminus
\{d_{\mathrm{gap}}\}$ (with structural gap at $d = k$), plus
the scalar contact term at $d = k + 1$. The depth spectrum
$\operatorname{Spec}(\widetilde{S}_k)$
(Computation~\ref{comp:m6-depth-spectrum} for $k = 6$)
records which depths are populated at each degree; this
combinatorial invariant is destroyed by symmetric-point
evaluation.

\textit{(ii) Palindrome structure.}
At degree~$4$, the full ordered polynomial factors through
$(\ell_1 - \ell_3)$ (equation~\eqref{eq:m4-full-palindrome}),
forcing diagonal vanishing $\widetilde{S}_4|_{\ell_1 = \ell_3}
= 0$. This palindrome factorisation of the spectral polynomial
is a reflection symmetry of the associahedron $K_4$ acting on
the ordered configurations; it persists at all even degrees
as the tree-reflection involution
$(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1}) \mapsto
(\lambda_{k-1}, \ldots, \lambda_1)$ (proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}). The scalar shadow $S_r$
at the symmetric point $\ell_1 = \ell_2 = \ell_3$ sees only
the consequence (the vanishing of certain coefficients), not
the cause (the palindrome factor).

\textit{(iii) Period-$2$ parity pattern.}
At even degrees $k \ge 4$, depths $d = 0$ and $d = 1$ of
$\widetilde{S}_k|_T$ vanish by the palindrome involution
(Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}(i)); at odd degrees, all
depths are populated. This period-$2$ oscillation is a
property of the \emph{polynomial} $\widetilde{S}_k$, visible
in the depth filtration of the ordered shadow. The
symmetric-point value $S_r$ retains the quantitative consequence
(certain rational functions of $c$ vanish) but not the structural
mechanism (the involution on binary trees).

\textit{(iv) Field-valued coefficients.}
At each depth~$d$, the coefficient of the degree-$d$ spectral
monomial in $\widetilde{S}_k$ is a \emph{field}: $\partial^j T$
with $j = k - 1 - d$. These field coefficients are
$c$-independent polynomials in $T$ and its derivatives
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-c-linearity}), growing as
$C^k \cdot k!$ (Gevrey-$1$, Theorem~\ref{thm:convergence-dichotomy}(ii)).
The Catalan symmetric-point values
$P_{2r+1}(1, \ldots, 1) = (-1)^{r-1} C_{r-1} \cdot (2r+1)!/2$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}(iv)) are the trace of the
field-weighted ordered polynomial at odd degrees.

\textit{The $E_1$ vs.\ $E_\infty$ content.}
The descent ${\Barch}^{\mathrm{ord}}_k(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \to
\Barch_k(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ to the symmetric bar
(Proposition~\ref{prop:r-matrix-descent})
takes $R$-matrix-twisted $\Sigma_k$-coinvariants.
Under this descent, the ordered shadow polynomial
$\widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})$ maps to a
symmetric function of $k$ variables, and the
extraction of the scalar component at the symmetric point
produces $S_r$. The depth filtration, palindrome structure,
and period-$2$ pattern are all destroyed by the
symmetrisation: they live in the kernel of the descent map
${\Barch}^{\mathrm{ord}} \to \Barch$, which is the
$E_1$-surplus (the additional data carried by the ordered bar
over the symmetric bar;
Remark~\ref{rem:two-colour-architecture}). The
symmetric bar sees only the scalar shadow $S_r$; the ordered bar
sees the full polynomial $\widetilde{S}_k$.

In the gravitational context: the scalar shadow $S_r$
determines the $r$-graviton scattering amplitude at a single
kinematic point ($s$-$t$-$u$ symmetric); the ordered shadow
$\widetilde{S}_k$ determines the full amplitude as a function
of all independent Mandelstam invariants. The soft graviton
hierarchy of
Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-infinite-soft-tower} is controlled
by the scalar shadow $S_r$; the full graviton
\emph{amplitude} at each degree is controlled by
$\widetilde{S}_k$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Genus-$1$ Catalan correction]
\label{rem:genus-1-catalan-correction}%
\index{Catalan number!genus-1 correction|textbf}%
\index{quasi-modular form!shadow correction}%
\index{G2 Eisenstein@$G_2$ Eisenstein series!shadow correction}
The genus-$0$ Catalan numbers $C_n$, governing the depth-$0$
layer of the ordered shadow and the field polynomial
(Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}), are \emph{not} preserved
at genus~$1$. The genus-$1$ curved bar differential
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{\,2} = \kappa\,\omega_1$ introduces a correction:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus-1-catalan-effective}
C_n^{\mathrm{eff}}(\tau)
\;=\;
C_n + \alpha_n\, G_2(\tau) + \beta_n\, G_4(\tau),
\end{equation}
where $G_2, G_4$ are the Eisenstein series and
$\{\alpha_n\}_{n \ge 1} = \{-\tfrac{5}{3},\,
-\tfrac{47}{10},\, -\tfrac{429}{35},\,
-\tfrac{10501}{252},\, \ldots\}$ is a $c$-independent sequence
that is \emph{not} a standard Catalan transform (it does not
satisfy the Catalan convolution $C_n = \sum C_i C_{n-1-i}$).
The correction is quasi-modular: the $G_2$ anomaly arises
from $c_0 = \{a_{(0)}b\} \neq 0$ (the first-order OPE coefficient),
which couples to the quasi-periodic defect of the
Weierstrass $\zeta$-function on the genus-$1$ sewing torus.
When $c_0 = 0$ (e.g.\ Heisenberg with its abelian Lie
bracket), $G_2$ does not enter and the
correction reduces to the holomorphic $G_4$ term alone.
The $c$-independence of $\alpha_n$ is the genus-$1$ avatar of the
$c$-independence theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-c-linearity}): the tree structure
of the resolvent is $c$-invariant, and the genus-$1$
correction inherits this invariance.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Novelty of the higher soft shadows]
The algebraic soft-shadow classes at order $S^{(p)}$ for
$p \ge 3$ are conditional predictions of the HT/celestial bridge.
They are not asserted here as established physical four-dimensional
soft theorems.  The first new algebraic prediction is the quintic
shadow class from $\mathfrak{S}_5$.
\end{remark}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{cllll}
\textbf{Soft order} &
\textbf{Shadow} &
\textbf{$\Ainf$ source} &
\textbf{Gauge status} &
\textbf{Physical interpretation} \\
\hline
$S^{(0)}$ & $S_2|_{\text{simple pole}}$ & $m_2$ &
 Non-trivial & Weinberg \\[2pt]
$S^{(1)}$ & $S_2|_{\text{double pole}}$ & $m_2$ &
 Non-trivial & Cachazo--Strominger \\[2pt]
$S^{(2)}$ & $S_3$ (primary), $S_4$ (graviton) &
 $m_3$, $m_4$ & Gauge-trivial / non-trivial &
 Cachazo--He--Yuan \\[2pt]
$S^{(3)}$ & $S_5$ & $m_5$ via $o_5 \neq 0$ &
 Non-trivial & Conditional quintic shadow \\[2pt]
$S^{(p)}$ & $S_{p+2}$ & $m_{p+2}$ via $o_{p+2}$ &
 Non-trivial for $p$ even &
 Conditional higher shadows
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{remark}[Semiclassical hierarchy]
At large $c$ ($G \to 0$): $S^{(0)}$ and $S^{(1)}$ are exact
(order $G^0$); $S^{(2)}_{\text{contact}} \sim 2/c^2$
(order $G^2$); $S_5 \sim -48/(5c^3)$
(order $G^3$).
The entire infinite algebraic shadow tower beyond $S^{(1)}$ is invisible
classically and constitutes a conditional prediction of the
$\Ainf$ structure. At $c = 26$ (critical string),
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = 0$ kills the genus tower, but the
soft-shadow hierarchy persists: the shadow classes are genus-$0$
kinematic data, while the genus tower is dynamical (all genera).
\end{remark}

%====================================================================
% THE BAR COMPLEX AND THE CONFORMAL BOOTSTRAP
%====================================================================

\subsection{The bar complex and the conformal bootstrap}
\label{subsec:bar-bootstrap}
\index{conformal bootstrap!from bar complex|textbf}
\index{crossing symmetry!from Stasheff identity|textbf}
\index{bootstrap bounds!from Shapovalov form}

The soft graviton hierarchy extracted the $\Ainf$ tower's
kinematic content. The conformal bootstrap is the dynamical
counterpart: it constrains and determines the OPE coefficients
and correlation functions of the boundary theory. The bar
complex produces both.

The conformal bootstrap programme constrains CFT data
$(\Delta_i, C_{ijk})$ by imposing crossing symmetry and unitarity
on four-point functions. The bar complex \emph{produces} CFT data
from the chiral algebra. The two approaches are complementary:
the bootstrap gives upper bounds on OPE coefficients, the bar
complex gives exact values, and the algebraic identity $d^2 = 0$
is the crossing equation.

\subsubsection*{OPE coefficients as collision residues}

The binary $\Ainf$ operation $m_2(\phi_i, \phi_j;\,\lambda)
= \sum_k C^k_{ij}(\lambda)\,\phi_k$ extracts the structure
constants $C^k_{ij}(\lambda)$ as collision residues of the bar
differential on $\FM_2(\C)$. For the Virasoro algebra with
$\phi_1 = T$ (the unique generator), the OPE coefficients are
read off directly from~\eqref{eq:gravity-m2}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bootstrap-ope-coefficients}
C^T_{TT} = 2\lambda, \qquad
C^{\partial T}_{TT} = 1, \qquad
C^{\mathrm{vac}}_{TT} = \frac{c}{12}\,\lambda^3.
\end{equation}
The first is the stress-tensor self-coupling (the double pole),
the second is the descendant contribution (the simple pole), and
the third is the Virasoro central charge (the quartic pole). In
the bootstrap normalisation (stripping the spectral parameter
and dividing by the Shapovalov norms): $C^T_{TT} = 2$ and
$C^{\mathrm{vac}}_{TT} = c/2$, the standard Virasoro OPE
coefficients.

\subsubsection*{Crossing symmetry as the Stasheff identity}

\begin{theorem}[Crossing = $d_{\barB}^2 = 0$; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:crossing-stasheff}%
\index{crossing symmetry!as Stasheff identity|textbf}%
The Stasheff identity at degree~$3$ on the bar element
$[s^{-1}\phi_i \mid s^{-1}\phi_j \mid s^{-1}\phi_k]$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:stasheff-crossing}
\sum_{\ell}\!\Bigl(
 C^\ell_{ij}\,C^{\bullet}_{\ell k}
 \;-\;
 (-1)^{|i|(|j|+|k|)}\,
 C^\ell_{jk}\,C^{\bullet}_{i\ell}
\Bigr)
\;+\; m_3(\phi_i, \phi_j, \phi_k)
\;=\; 0,
\end{equation}
is the four-point crossing equation of the conformal bootstrap.
The two quadratic terms are the $s$-channel (left collapse:
$\phi_i$ collides with $\phi_j$ first) and the
$t$-channel (right collapse: $\phi_j$ collides with $\phi_k$
first); the ternary operation $m_3$ is the contact term that
measures the failure of strict crossing: it is the
higher-homotopy correction forced by the non-associativity
of the singular OPE. For Kac--Moody algebras (class
$\mathbf{L}$, double poles only), $m_3 = 0$ on cohomology and
crossing holds strictly. For Virasoro (class $\mathbf{M}$,
quartic pole), $m_3 \ne 0$
\textup{(}\eqref{eq:gravity-m3}\textup{)} and crossing is
satisfied only up to the contact correction.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The degree-$3$ bar differential acts on the degree-$3$ element
$[s^{-1}\phi_i \mid s^{-1}\phi_j \mid s^{-1}\phi_k]$ by
\[
d_{\barB}^2 = 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
(m_2 \circ_1 m_2 - m_2 \circ_2 m_2 + d \circ m_3
 + m_3 \circ d)
 [\phi_i \mid \phi_j \mid \phi_k] = 0.
\]
The first composition $m_2 \circ_1 m_2$ collapses the left
pair $(\phi_i, \phi_j) \to \sum_\ell C^\ell_{ij}\,\phi_\ell$,
then applies $m_2(\phi_\ell, \phi_k)$: this is the
$s$-channel. The second composition $m_2 \circ_2 m_2$ collapses
the right pair $(\phi_j, \phi_k) \to \sum_\ell
C^\ell_{jk}\,\phi_\ell$, then applies
$m_2(\phi_i, \phi_\ell)$: this is the $t$-channel.
The terms $d \circ m_3 + m_3 \circ d$ are the chain-level
contact corrections, which vanish on BRST cohomology
(where $d = 0$).

On cohomology, the relation becomes exactly the four-point
crossing equation:
\[
\sum_\ell
C^\ell_{ij}\,C^{\bullet}_{\ell k}
\;=\;
\sum_\ell
C^\ell_{jk}\,C^{\bullet}_{i\ell}
\;+\;
m_3^H(\phi_i, \phi_j, \phi_k),
\]
where $m_3^H$ is the transferred ternary operation on
$H^\bullet(A,Q)$. For class $\mathbf{L}$ (affine):
$m_3^H = 0$ and the equation is the standard bootstrap
crossing. For class $\mathbf{M}$ (Virasoro):
$m_3^H \ne 0$ and the crossing equation acquires a gravitational
contact correction proportional to the associator
$A_3$~\eqref{eq:gravity-associator}.

The geometric content: the codimension-$1$ boundary of $\FM_3(\C)$
has two strata, $D_{\{1,2\}}$ and $D_{\{2,3\}}$, corresponding
to the $s$- and $t$-channels. Stokes' theorem
$\int_{\FM_3} d\omega_3 = \int_{D_{\{1,2\}}} \omega_3
- \int_{D_{\{2,3\}}} \omega_3 = 0$ is the crossing equation.
The $u$-channel ($D_{\{1,3\}}$) is not independent: it is a
linear combination of $s$ and $t$ by the FM boundary relations
(cf.\ the proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:YBE}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The $\Ainf$ tower solves the full bootstrap hierarchy]
\label{rem:ainf-solves-bootstrap}%
\index{bootstrap!solved by $\Ainf$ tower}%
The crossing equation at degree~$3$ is only the first level.
At each degree~$n$, the Stasheff identity
$\sum_{i+j=n+1}(-1)^{i(j-1)} m_i \circ m_j = 0$ is the
$(n+1)$-point crossing equation on $\FM_n(\C)$, expressing the
consistency of all $n$-point OPE channels. The $\Ainf$
structure $\{m_k\}_{k \ge 2}$ is precisely a \emph{solution} to
the full infinite hierarchy of crossing equations: it is the
unique (up to gauge equivalence) $\Ainf$ structure extending the
binary OPE. The bar complex therefore
\textbf{solves the conformal bootstrap at all $n$-point
levels simultaneously}, with the solution being the complete
$\Ainf$ tower. For Virasoro, this is the infinite tower
$\{m_k\}_{k \ge 2}$ of Movement~I.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Unitarity and the Shapovalov form}

\begin{theorem}[Bootstrap bounds from the Shapovalov form;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:bootstrap-shapovalov}%
\index{Shapovalov form!bootstrap bounds|textbf}%
\index{unitarity!from Shapovalov form}%
The bar complex computes OPE coefficients on the full Verma module
$M_h$. Unitarity constraints enter through the Shapovalov form
$\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\mathrm{Shap}}$ on $M_h$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The transferred operation $m_k^H$ on BRST cohomology
 $H^\bullet(A,Q)$ is computed by the HPL transfer through the
 strong deformation retract $(V, H^0, i, p, h)$, where
 $h$ is the Shapovalov projector onto the complement of
 quasi-primaries. The denominators of $m_k^H$ are the Kac
 determinants $\det_N\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\mathrm{Shap}}$
 at levels $N \le k$
 \textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:gravity-c-linearity-physics})}.
\item For unitary representations ($c \ge 1$, $h \ge 0$; or
 $c = c_{p,q}$ with $h = h_{r,s}$), the Shapovalov form is
 positive definite on the irreducible quotient $L_h =
 M_h/\langle\text{null vectors}\rangle$. The transferred OPE
 coefficients $C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{unitary}}$ are obtained from
 $C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{Verma}}$ by projecting out null states.
 The projection can only \emph{reduce} the number of intermediate
 states in the crossing sum: hence
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:bootstrap-bound}
 |C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{unitary}}|^2
 \;\le\;
 |C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{Verma}}|^2,
 \end{equation}
 with equality when no null vectors contribute to the
 channel~$k$.
\item The Kac determinant poles at $c = c_{p,q}$ are the loci
 where null vectors appear and the Verma module is reducible.
 At these points, some OPE channels close (the structure
 constants vanish for null-state channels), and the crossing
 equations acquire additional constraints: these are the
 \emph{minimal-model bootstrap equations}. The bar complex
 encodes this as the appearance of poles in $m_k^H$ at
 the Kac-table values, subsequently cancelled by the
 Stasheff relations
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:stasheff-cancellation})}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(i) is the content of
Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-c-linearity-physics}: the HPL transfer
introduces $1/\det_N(\mathrm{Shap})$ at each level~$N$ through
the homotopy~$h$.

(ii): On the Verma module $M_h$, the crossing sum
$\sum_\ell C^\ell_{ij}\,\bar C^{\ell}_{ij}$ runs over all states
$|\ell\rangle \in M_h$. On the irreducible quotient $L_h$,
null states $|\chi\rangle$ (satisfying
$\langle\chi|\chi\rangle_{\mathrm{Shap}} = 0$) are modded out.
The projection $M_h \twoheadrightarrow L_h$ is orthogonal with
respect to the Shapovalov form: it removes positive-semidefinite
contributions from the crossing sum. Hence the unitary OPE
coefficients are bounded above by the Verma-module values.

(iii): At $c = c_{p,q}$, the Kac determinant
$\det_N(\mathrm{Shap}) = \prod_{rs \le N}
(h - h_{r,s}(c))^{p(N-rs)}$ vanishes. The null vector
$|\chi_{r,s}\rangle$ decouples: the structure constant
$C^{\chi_{r,s}}_{ij} = 0$ by the null-state Ward identity.
This decoupling is visible in the bar complex as the cancellation
of Kac-table poles in the shadow obstruction tower
(Theorem~\ref{thm:stasheff-cancellation}).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The large-$c$ bootstrap from the shadow obstruction tower}

\begin{proposition}[Large-$c$ expansion from the shadow obstruction tower;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:large-c-bootstrap}%
\index{large-$c$ expansion!from shadow tower|textbf}%
\index{conformal bootstrap!large-$c$}%
At $c \to \infty$ ($G \to 0$, semiclassical gravity), the shadow
tower organises into a $1/c$ expansion that matches the large-$c$
conformal bootstrap:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Leading order.)}
 $S_2 = \kappa = c/2$, the modular characteristic of the
 Virasoro algebra.
 In the bootstrap, this controls the normalisation of the
 stress-tensor two-point function
 $\langle T(z)T(0)\rangle = c/(2z^4)$:
 the Weinberg soft factor.
\item \textup{(First correction.)}
 $S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)] \sim 2/c^2$ at large $c$.
 This is the first non-trivial contact invariant: the
 quartic correction to the four-point graviton amplitude.
 In the bootstrap, it corresponds to the $O(1/c^2)$
 correction to the four-point function from the identity
 Virasoro block~\textup{\cite{HR09}}.
\item \textup{(Systematic expansion.)}
 For $r \ge 4$: $S_r \sim \mathrm{const}/c^{r-2}$
 \textup{(}the large-$c$ column in the shadow table,
 \S\textup{\ref{subsec:gravity-soft-theorems})}.
 The $n$-th order correction to the
 bootstrap is controlled by $S_{n+2}$: the shadow obstruction tower
 IS the $1/c$ expansion of the bootstrap. The
 convergence radius $R_{\mathrm{scal}}
 = c\sqrt{(5c+22)/(180c+872)} \to \infty$ as $c \to \infty$:
 the perturbative expansion is summable in the semiclassical
 limit.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The large-$c$ asymptotics of $S_r$ follow from the shadow
metric $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = (c+6t)^2 + 80t^2/(5c+22)$.
At large $c$: $Q(t) \approx c^2 + 12ct + 36t^2 = (c+6t)^2$,
so $\sqrt{Q} \approx c + 6t$ and
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q} \approx ct^2 + 6t^3$.
The corrections to $\sqrt{Q}$ are $O(t^2/c)$:
$\sqrt{Q} = c + 6t + 40t^2/[c(5c+22)] + \cdots$,
giving $S_r = [t^r]H/r$ with $[t^r]H = O(c^{3-r})$ for
$r \ge 4$. The convergence radius is
$R_{\mathrm{scal}} = |t_\pm|
= c\sqrt{(5c+22)/(180c+872)} \sim c/\sqrt{36} = c/6$ at
large~$c$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The modular bootstrap from the genus tower}

\begin{remark}[Modular bootstrap = MCG equivariance of the
genus-$1$ bar complex]
\label{rem:modular-bootstrap-bar}%
\index{modular bootstrap!from genus-$1$ bar complex|textbf}%
\index{MCG equivariance!modular bootstrap}%
The modular bootstrap constrains the genus-$1$ partition function
$Z(\tau) = \mathrm{tr}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$ by requiring modular
invariance under $\mathrm{SL}(2,\Z)$. In the bar-complex
language: the genus-$1$ MC element
$\Theta^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$ lives on the bordered FM
compactification $\overline{C}{}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k,\vec{m}}$
at genus~$1$, and the mapping class group
$\mathrm{MCG}(\Sigma_{1,1}) \simeq \mathrm{SL}(2,\Z)$ acts on
the genus-$1$ sector of the modular bar coalgebra. The MC
equation at genus~$1$, combined with the equivariance of the bar
construction under this action
(Proposition~\ref{V1-prop:mcg-equivariance-tower}), forces
$Z(\tau)$ to be modular invariant.

The modular bootstrap is therefore not an independent constraint
but a \emph{consequence} of the bar-complex structure:
$d_{\barB}^2 = \kappa\cdot\omega_1$ at genus~$1$ encodes both
the curvature (which determines $Z(\tau) = \eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}$)
and the modular anomaly (which constrains $Z$ to transform
with weight $-\kappa/2$ under $S$). At $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}
= (c-26)/2 = 0$: the modular bootstrap is trivially satisfied
($Z^{\mathrm{eff}} = 1$); at $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} \ne 0$:
the non-holomorphic completion
$\widehat{E}_2 = E_2 - 3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$
absorbs the anomaly
(Proposition~\ref{prop:genus1-modular-anomaly}). The annular
bar complex (Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential})
computes $Z(\tau)$ as the trace of the genus-$1$ annular MC
element, closing the circle:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Bootstrap datum} & \textbf{Bar-complex source}
 & \textbf{Eq.} \\
\hline
OPE coefficients $C^k_{ij}$
 & Collision residues of $d_{\barB}$ on $\FM_2$
 & \eqref{eq:bootstrap-ope-coefficients} \\
Crossing symmetry
 & Stasheff identity ($d_{\barB}^2 = 0$)
 & \eqref{eq:stasheff-crossing} \\
Unitarity bounds
 & Shapovalov quotient $M_h \twoheadrightarrow L_h$
 & \eqref{eq:bootstrap-bound} \\
Large-$c$ expansion
 & Shadow obstruction tower $S_r \sim c^{2-r}$
 & \eqref{eq:shadow-metric-Q} \\
Modular invariance
 & MCG equivariance of genus-$1$ $\Theta$
 & \eqref{eq:gravity-Z1} \\
Cardy density of states
 & Saddle-point of $S$-transformed $\Theta^{(1)}$
 & \eqref{eq:gravity-cardy} \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The conformal bootstrap is the shadow of the bar complex,
projected onto the space of crossing-symmetric, modular-invariant
correlation functions. The bar complex is the lift:
it provides the \emph{algebraic origin} of the constraints that
the bootstrap imposes, and simultaneously provides the
\emph{exact solution} that the bootstrap bounds.
\end{remark}

%====================================================================
% QUANTUM CHAOS DIAGNOSTICS FROM THE BAR COMPLEX
%====================================================================

\subsection{Quantum chaos diagnostics from the annular bar complex}
\label{subsec:quantum-chaos-bar}
\index{quantum chaos!from bar complex|textbf}
\index{spectral form factor!from annular bar complex|textbf}
\index{out-of-time-order correlator|textbf}
\index{Lyapunov exponent!MSS bound|textbf}
\index{scrambling time|textbf}

The bar complex carries the complete algebraic data of the
2d CFT; the annular bar complex
(Definition~\ref{def:annular-bar},
Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential})
computes the genus-$1$ partition function
$Z(\tau) = \Tr(q^{L_0 - c/24})$
as the trace of the genus-$1$ MC element. Quantum chaos
diagnostics (the spectral form factor (SFF), out-of-time-order
correlators (OTOCs), the Lyapunov exponent, and the scrambling
time) are derived quantities, all determined by the genus
tower and the $\Ainf$ structure. This section extracts them.

The key structural point: the bar complex does not merely
\emph{encode} quantum chaos diagnostics; it \emph{explains}
their algebraic origin. The MSS bound $\lambda_L \le 2\pi/\beta$
is a consequence of the curvature identity
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_1$, which forces the
saddle-point geometry of the $S$-transformed partition function.
The scrambling time $t_* \sim (\beta/2\pi)\log c$ is the
timescale at which the $1/c$ expansion of the shadow obstruction tower
(Proposition~\ref{prop:large-c-bootstrap}) breaks down. The ramp
